Germany Denies Transporting Munitions to Japan 66

National News Agency, Berlin, 23rd: Recently, Nanjing newspapers reported that Japan, due to its military invasion of eastern China, purchased a large amount of military supplies from Germany, and that German arsenals began working day and night to fulfill these orders and supplement their original workers. Those concerned here regard this report as completely unfounded. Since the end of the European War and the signing of the Treaty of Versailles, Germany has been prohibited from manufacturing munitions and transporting them to foreign countries. This is the most obvious fact. Currently, the authorities in various parts of Germany are consistently implementing this prohibition, so there is absolutely no matter of selling military supplies to Japan. However, foreign ships sometimes transport military supplies produced by other countries through German ports, leading to suspicions that they came from Germany. In fact, these ships were already carrying munitions when they passed through Germany, and Germany has no way to prohibit them.

Former Austrian Prime Minister Schober Seriously Ill 67

National News Agency, Vienna, 23rd: Former Austrian Prime Minister Schober recently contracted heart disease, and his condition is very critical. The matter is causing considerable concern in all sectors.

Public Telegram 68

Telegram from Jingdezhen: To all newspapers, please note: We recently sent a telegram to the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Finance, which reads: "Investigation reveals that the special production and sales tax on porcelain, etc., levied by the Jiangxi Provincial Government is a disguised form of likin, violating the National Government's clear order to abolish likin and contradicting the established policy of abolishing likin and increasing taxes. The people of Jiangxi, already impoverished, find it extremely difficult to bear this harsh tax. The people of Jiangxi, through various organizations and affiliated associations, have repeatedly telegraphed your departments, requesting the prohibition of this tax. Currently, Director of the Collection Bureau, Xiu Siyong, has led more than one hundred staff members from the province to the town, disregarding the strong opposition of the local people and forcibly establishing bureaus and checkpoints to detain porcelain ships, leading to a porcelain merchant strike and kiln owners shutting down operations. More than one hundred thousand unemployed workers are marching and petitioning, which is likely to cause a major crisis. Moreover, Jingdezhen borders bandit areas, and alarms are frequent. We are deeply concerned that the unrest will escalate and disrupt local security. The consequences are unimaginable. In addition to reporting to the party and government authorities, we urgently request your departments to examine and approve, and immediately telegraph the Jiangxi Provincial Government to abolish the special production and sales tax on porcelain, etc., on a fixed date. The porcelain industry will be fortunate, and the local area will be fortunate." This town has suffered repeated bandit raids in recent years, and porcelain production has plummeted. Today, the Jiangxi Provincial Government is levying harsh taxes on this dying national product, causing a major disturbance and endangering the life of national porcelain. We urgently request assistance in order to achieve the goal of abolishing the tax. We are greatly looking forward to your assistance. Jingdezhen General Chamber of Commerce respectfully prays.

Important News

Japanese Military Invasion of Jehol Province 69

Jehol Troops Resist Japanese Aggression and Retreat

Tang Pinglin Dispatches Dong's Brigade to Reinforce Chaoyang

According to reports from Beiping, following the clash between Japanese and Jehol troops in the area between Chaoyang Temple and Beipiao on the 18th, inquiries were made to Jehol by Beiping officials on the 19th and 20th. The results proved that there was no fighting on those two days because the Japanese military ceased their military actions, so our troops also ceased resistance. However, yesterday (21st), the Japanese side publicized that representatives of the Jehol authorities were in contact with Japanese representatives to negotiate the rescue of Ishimoto and the restoration of the Beipiao branch line. Officials stated that they had not yet received formal reports and had telegraphed to inquire about the truth. However, it is generally speculated that the situation on the Jehol border has indeed eased and negotiations may be in progress. The following is a record of the Japanese military invasion of Jehol:

Ishimoto Goes Missing: The Japanese Yoda Brigade stationed in Jinxi, using the disappearance of the Japanese Ishimoto Kenshiro as an excuse, dispatched armored vehicles and air squadrons on the 18th to begin attacking the Jehol border. The air squadron also flew to Chaoyang and dropped more than 30 bombs. Official reports detailing our losses and the details of the conflict at Chaoyang Temple were received yesterday (21st). The Japanese Ishimoto Kenshiro was originally a businessman in Beipiao. After the Japanese military occupied Jinxi, the Japanese commander stationed in Jinxi appointed him as a military transport liaison officer, responsible for transportation on the South Manchuria Railway. Whether Ishimoto had recently been to Beipiao was not notified to the Jehol Provincial Government or the Japanese Consul stationed in Chifeng. If Ishimoto went to Jehol, he would have to obtain a residency passport from the consulate and, at the same time, notify local officials according to procedures. Since the location of Ishimoto's disappearance was within Liaoning territory, Jehol was unaware beforehand and naturally cannot be held responsible.

Japanese Military Opens Fire: At the same time, the Japanese, using the excuse that military trains were attacked by righteous volunteers, dispatched two armored trains carrying over 1,000 Japanese soldiers and equipped with 15-centimeter heavy artillery from the Japanese brigade headquarters in Jin County at 2:00 PM on the 18th. They drove into Chaoyang Temple Station, forcibly trying to head to Beipiao. At that time, the commander of the first battalion of Dong's brigade, Zhang Shouzhen, was responsible for protecting the railway from Chaoyang Temple to Beipiao. Commander Zhang believed that the Japanese armored trains were forcibly trying to head to Beipiao, and his troops had not received orders, so he immediately stopped them. The Japanese armored trains first fired more than ten shots as a show of force, intending to intimidate our small number of troops.

Our Troops Resist: At that time, Commander Zhang was about to negotiate with the Japanese officers on the armored trains when the Japanese suddenly opened fire with machine guns. Our side immediately resisted, and a fierce battle broke out. The location was near Chaoyang Temple. By 8:00 PM, the Jehol troops, due to their weak strength, concentrated all their forces on Nanling. Nanling is an important mountainous area on the Jinxi-Chaoyang branch line. There is a tunnel under the mountain through which trains can reach Beipiao. Due to the fierce resistance of our troops, the Japanese armored trains retreated to Chaoyang Temple Station and returned to Jin County. Commander Zhang's left leg was indeed slightly injured. The above is the actual situation of the conflict on the Jehol border.

Chaoyang Bombed: Regarding the bombing of Chaoyang by Japanese aircraft, according to County Magistrate Li's report, Japanese aircraft dropped a total of 34 bombs on the brigade headquarters, telegraph bureau, and mortar company in the county town. Among them, three mortar shells did not explode. Our side was caught off guard and did not have time to prepare. More than 30 soldiers and civilians were killed or injured, and more than ten military horses of the brigade headquarters were also killed. On the 19th, the Japanese military took no action. The Japanese brigade headquarters stationed in Jin County sent Staff Officer Yoshioka and Muta, the Japanese consul stationed in Chifeng, to the Jehol garrison to request that the disappearance of Ishimoto be investigated. It is said that Jehol Chairman Tang Yulin has dispatched Dong Futing's brigade to Chaoyang due to the Japanese military's harassment of the border.

Situation Eases: Yesterday (21st) at 4:00 PM, Meng Zhaotian, Jehol's military representative and deputy director of political training, personally used a long-distance telephone to inquire with Jehol. According to the reply, there was nothing wrong on the Jehol border today (21st), and the situation has eased. The Jehol troops are still at Nanling, and the Japanese military has not crossed the Jehol border by even one step. Chairman Tang is currently in Chengde, etc. This proves that the area east of Chaoyang is peaceful and without incident. As for the disappearance of Ishimoto, it will be clarified within a few days. The Jehol troops are also maintaining a considerable level of alert in the Beipiao area. As of the evening of the 20th, the Beipiao branch line train has not yet resumed traffic.

Tang Resolves to Resist: Yesterday, this reporter interviewed Meng Zhaotian, Jehol's military political training deputy supervisor and military representative, asking about the recent situation in Jehol Province. Meng made the following important remarks: This time, the Japanese military, using the Ishimoto disappearance issue as an excuse, dispatched five aircraft to Chaoyang to bomb at 2:00 PM on the 18th. The circumstances of our losses have been reported to me by Chairman Tang in a telegram. At the same time, military action also occurred at Chaoyang Temple Station, which is connected to Liaoning Province. Two Japanese armored trains forcibly tried to pass through and head to Beipiao. Our troops stopped them, and the Japanese military suddenly opened fire. Our troops had no choice but to resist. In the past two days, I have inquired with Song Juchuan, the director of the Jehol long-distance telephone bureau, via long-distance telephone. According to Director Song, the border area of Chaoyang Temple Beipiao is peaceful and the situation has eased. Our military defense is very solid. Chairman Tang Yulin believes that if the Japanese military invades Jehol territory, he will resolutely resist. Currently, the main force of our army has been concentrated at a suitable location. Chairman Tang has recently stated, "I have lived to be over sixty years old and will never commit acts of treason or betrayal. I do not want to be ridiculed by the world." (22nd)

After the League of Nations Investigative Mission Arrived in Beiping 70

They Will Organize Materials and Prepare a Report

The Mission Is Highly Attentive to the Jehol Issue

According to reports from Beiping, the League of Nations Investigative Mission, consisting of more than twenty people, arrived in Jinan from Qingdao on the morning of the 20th and then split up to go to Beiping. Lytton and the French member, along with our Chinese representative Gu Weijun, flew north by plane, arriving at 11:00 AM that morning. After disembarking, Lytton, feeling slightly unwell, immediately took a car to the German Hospital to rest. The French member took a car to the Beijing Hotel, and Representative Gu also returned to his private residence in Tieshizi Hutong. The German, American, and Italian members, as well as the Japanese representative Yoshida and his entourage, also took a special train on the Tianjin-Pukou Railway from Jinan on the morning of the same day, arriving in Tianjin at 5:45 PM. They stopped for more than twenty minutes and then headed north to Beiping, arriving at 9:10 PM. It is reported that the attitude of each member upon returning from Japan is very different from that before going to Japan, perhaps due to the stimulation of the Japanese attitude. A representative stated that the steps planned by the investigation mission have achieved very few objectives and are very unsatisfactory. It is determined that the investigation mission report will be completed by the end of August. Furthermore, according to a spokesperson for the investigative mission who spoke to reporters, the materials obtained by the investigative mission in its investigation in the three northeastern provinces are still being organized and will be completed in the near future. The organization work is being carried out separately by the various expert members in cooperation with the secretaries. After all the materials have been organized, a drafting committee will be organized by the members to hold a meeting and discuss, and then work will begin on the preparation of the report. Currently, in terms of the time spent on organizing the materials, the drafting of the report will probably have to wait another ten days or so. Therefore, this is still the secretarial work period. After ten days, it will be the members' work period. It is believed that within ten days, each member may go to Beidaihe one after another in order to allocate work at that time. The Chinese side has submitted more than twenty types of memoranda to the investigative mission, and it is said that a small portion has not yet been delivered, and the number is unknown. The Japanese side has also submitted memoranda, all for the investigative mission's reference. The investigation mission is paying close attention to the problems that have occurred on the Jehol border, but it cannot make any comments. (22nd)

The Jiangxi, Guangdong, and Hunan Armies Launch a General Offensive Against the Communist Bandits in Southern Jiangxi 71

Troops from Five Provinces Encircle and Suppress the Communists on the Border of Jiangxi, Guangdong, and Fujian

Aimed at Meeting in Ruijin, the Fake Communist Capital

According to reports from Nanchang, a letter was recently received from Ganzhou stating that the Communist bandits who invaded Guangdong have been severely suppressed by the Guangdong army, suffering heavy losses. They have completely withdrawn to the areas of Xinfeng, Anyuan, Xunwu, and Huichang, with the bandits in western Fujian and eastern Jiangxi coordinating with each other. Although there are still remnants of bandits in Guangdong, they are covering the withdrawal of the Communist masses to Jiangxi. Currently, the three divisions of Zhou Zhirou, Liu Shaoxian, and Li Ming of the 18th Army of Jiangxi have fully arrived in Nankang and Dayu. In addition to stationing a portion of their troops in Ganzhou to secure the rear, the rest have joined the front lines. Wang Dongyuan's division of the Hunan Army, which advanced from Chongyi to Dayu, has also been incorporated into the battle sequence. It is said that the divisions of Miao Pei-nan, Zhang Da, Li Han, Wang Zanbin, etc. of the Guangdong and Guangxi armies have also completed their deployment and will launch a general offensive against the bandits in Xinfeng. The Guangdong army, with Miao Pei-nan's department as the vanguard, has already begun fighting at the junction of Nanxiong and Xinfeng. The Jiangxi and Hunan armies will launch a two-pronged attack from Nankang and Dayu to the northwest of Xinfeng. According to aerial reconnaissance reports, the bandits in Xinfeng and Sannan are covering the transport of baggage, heavy artillery, and looted supplies to Ruijin and Ningdu. The stretcher teams are continuously moving northeast from the Guangdong border. The Communist masses have no intention of fighting and seem to have other plans. However, the Central Government has made a final decision to suppress the bandits, and Chen Jitang of Guangdong has deeply realized that the Guangdong army must unite with the Central Army to suppress the bandits due to the losses of the Guangdong army in southern Jiangxi. Therefore, the armies of the five provinces of Hunan, Jiangxi, Guangdong, Guangxi, and Fujian have agreed to act in unison. Upon investigation of the defense lines of each province, the Guangdong border starts at Nanxiong and extends west to the Hunan border in Renhua and Lechang, and east through Lianping, Heping, Pingyuan, and Jiaoling to Heping in Fujian. This line is defended by the three armies of Xiang Hanping, Li Yangjing, and Yu Hanmou, and Wang Zanbin's division of the Guangxi army. The Jiangxi border starts at Dayu and extends from Nankang and Ganxian along the east bank of the Gan River through Wanbao, Xinghe, Ji'an, and Jishui, and then from Jishui, Yongfeng, Xiang'an, Xinghuang, and Nanfeng counties diagonally eastward to Jianning in Fujian. This line is extremely long. The area above Ganzhou is entirely defended by the 18th Army, and the area below Ganzhou and reaching Ji'an is defended by Wang Liande's troops. The area west from Yongfeng and east to Nanfeng, crossing the central part of Jiangxi Province, is guarded by the armies of Hao Menglin, Sun Lianzhong, and Mao Bingwen. On the Fujian Province side, its defense line against the bandits starts from Jianning and extends along Zhangping to Zhangzhou, and then through Yunxiao, Kehe, and connects with the Guangdong Eastern Jiang garrison. The 19th Route Army is the main attacking force. The above-mentioned forces from the five provinces, at least twenty or more divisions and approximately 200,000 or more men, will form a large encirclement around the Communist bandits on the border of Jiangxi, Guangdong, and Fujian, with Ruijin and Tingzhou as the meeting point. If a quick and complete victory can be achieved, the Communist bandits will definitely be eliminated. (July 22nd)

Fujian Province's Education Funds and Finances 72

The Education Fund Committee Proposes Guiding Principles

The Province's Finances Are Divided into Three Districts for Reorganization

According to reports from Fuzhou, under the Red Peril and the Zhang forces' warlordism in Fujian, education funds and finances are truly in dire straits and extremely impoverished. The Provincial Government and the Education Fund Committee are therefore planning to reorganize the province's education funds and finances as much as possible. At 10:00 AM on the 16th of this month, the Education Fund Committee held a meeting in the Provincial Government Conference Room. Fang Shengtao, Cheng Shih-jui, Chen Peikun, Deraeburg, and others attended. First, Cheng Shih-jui, Director of the Education Department, reported on the difficulties in allocating education funds over the years. Then, Chen Peikun, Director of the Education Fund Management Office, reported on the income and expenditure of education funds. Deraeburg, the assistant auditor, stated that he strongly supports the protection of education funds and would never suppress, save, or misappropriate them. Finally, three guiding principles were agreed upon: (1) Education funds should be allocated monthly, with 120,000 yuan as the guiding principle; (2) Unless there are extreme difficulties with salt taxes, education funding should remain unchanged as the guiding principle; (3) If changes are unavoidable, the amount should be approved by the Education Fund Committee. In general, education funding may not be as difficult as before. As for the financial aspect, the Provincial Government Committee previously proposed a plan to reorganize the province's finances by dividing them into districts and submitted it for review. The general idea of the plan is to divide the province into three districts, with one commissioner assigned to each district, responsible for reorganizing various tax revenues in the district and remitting tax revenues to the Finance Department, and reporting the reorganization progress and tax revenue status to the Provincial Government at any time. On the 15th of this month, the Provincial Government Committee reviewed and discussed the plan to reorganize finances by dividing them into districts, and decided that the first district would be based on the prefectures of Ningde, Fuan, and Xiapu; the second district would be based on the prefectures of Yancheng, Jianning, and Shaowu and a part of the Tingzhou prefecture; and the third district would be based on the prefectures of Zhangzhou, Xiamen, Quanzhou, Yongchun, and Longyan. The detailed areas will be determined by a map. Each district will have one commissioner. The commissioners should be accompanied by staff selected from civil servants as a guiding principle. The rest will be handled according to the review report. However, the commissioner may establish an office in a suitable location in the district. The Provincial Government has also decided on the candidates for the commissioner: Shi Jialin (current Director of the Finance Department) will be the first district commissioner, Lin Jinan (current member of the Provincial Government) will be the second district commissioner, and He Gonggan (former Director of the Finance Department) will be the third district commissioner. An official order will be issued within a few days, and they will start working at the beginning of next month. (July 18th)

The Issue of the Qingdao Wharf Being Contracted to a Japanese Merchant 73

The Municipal Government Cleverly Defends Itself

The People Firmly Oppose

According to reports from Qingdao, the Municipal Government decided to contract the construction of the No. 5 Wharf of the Great Harbor in this city to the Japanese merchant Fukuchang Company. Although it has been repeatedly and firmly opposed by citizens of the city and people from all over the country, the Municipal Government still cleverly defends itself, claiming that although the project is contracted to a Japanese merchant, the rights and interests have not been transferred to foreigners. Because the contract stipulates that local Chinese workers must be hired, the cement is limited to Qixin's "Horse Brand," the stone is Laushan's granite, and the wood is Singapore's red hardwood. In fact, it is no different from Chinese people doing it themselves. However, may I ask, if our country's politics are also managed by the Japanese, and our Chinese people still eat rice and goods grown by Chinese farmers and use Chinese workers, how is this different from the facts? What should we say about this? Moreover, upon investigation, during the Japanese administration of Qingdao, they planned to repair and dredge the No. 1 Wharf of the Great Harbor and had already produced 624 large concrete blocks, each weighing 60 tons, but they were never used. When we took over Jiao'ao in the twelfth year, our Jiao'ao Public Administration bought them at the price of one million yuan in national currency. Unexpectedly, these blocks were never used, and most of them have been crushed and broken. They are currently piled up on the vacant land behind the Naval Factory in this city. Although our country has wasted a million yuan on this useless waste, it is fortunate that it has not been used for construction. Otherwise, once used, it would be difficult to guarantee that there would be no danger from the impact of the tide. Furthermore, although it is stipulated that Laushan gravel and Qixin cement should be used for this No. 5 Wharf, how can we know that they will not be replaced with Japanese cement and inferior gravel? The Municipal Government also said that the Japanese merchant Fukuchang Company won the bid with 3.9 million yuan. It is rumored that Kang Yi's bid price was 3.95 million yuan, including 60,000 yuan for underwater engineering excavation costs. The actual bid price was 3.89 million yuan. Therefore, various rumors have arisen, slandering the Municipal Government. Bao Kangyi does not specify 60,000 yuan for underwater engineering in its bid, which is purely a rumor, and there are various merchants' bids that can prove it. Regarding this point, the various Shanghai groups and the National Salvation

Page 8

Joint Conference once sent someone to Kang Yi's office to check the duplicate of the bid review, which clearly stated that the excavation cost for underwater engineering was five yuan per cubic meter, totaling 60,000 yuan. Moreover, Kang Yi had sent a letter to the Qingdao Municipal Government's Purchasing Committee explaining the necessity of the excavation. This point is an extremely important contribution to the project. In principle, the Municipal Government should be grateful for it, but now it is said to be creating rumors, what is the intention? It is inexplicable. Kang Yi has contracted many huge projects in Shanghai and has always had extremely harmonious feelings with our Chinese people, and one-third or more of the shares are held by Chinese people. How can there be such a thing as spreading rumors? Moreover, it has already been agreed with the Shanghai people that they would undertake it for 3.89 million yuan including excavation costs, but the Qingdao Municipal Government ignores this and disregards the people's opposition. I don't know what the intention of the officials of the Municipal Government is. I sincerely hope that the Municipal Government will give this issue very serious consideration.

The Opening of the National Postal Workers' Congress 74

More Than a Hundred Representatives Attend

The Second Congress of the National Postal Workers' Unions in various regions, after being renamed the Joint Discussion Conference of the National Postal Workers' Unions in various regions with the approval of the Central Government, has been decided to be held in the auditorium of the Capital YMCA. The opening ceremony was held at 9:00 AM today (24th). The formal meeting period is four days, and the closing ceremony is scheduled for the afternoon of the 28th. At the opening ceremony, representatives from the Central Government, the National Government, the Ministry of Communications, and the Capital Party and government agencies attended to provide guidance. More than one hundred representatives from 53 unions in more than 30 postal districts attended. The following is a record of the situation:

Congress Organization: The Congress has established a secretariat, which is divided into four departments: Documentation, Reception, Affairs, and Accounting. Zhao Sheng was appointed as the Secretary-General by the Preparatory Committee of the National Postal Workers' Union, Zhou Bingwen, Qiao Wenhuan, and Zhu Yinghua were appointed as Secretaries, Zhang Kechang was appointed as the Director of the Accounting Department, Kong Fanzao was appointed as the Director of the Documentation Department, Wang Shufan and Cao Jiaxiu were appointed as the Directors of the Reception Department, Wang Yisheng and Li Daming were appointed as the Directors of the Affairs Department, along with the staff of each department, totaling more than fifty employees. The General Office and the General Reception Office of the Secretariat are located at the Anle Hotel in the capital, and a branch reception office is located at the Southeast Hotel in Xiaguan. The Shanghai branch reception office is handled by the Shanghai Postal Workers' Union.

Registered Representatives: The General Association: Lu Jingshi, Zhu Xuefan, Wang Shufan, Wang Yisheng, Zhang Kechang, Zhao Shusheng, Zhu Yinghua; Hankou: Han Dayong, Chen Liang; Changsha: Xiao Yunhan, Yang Shoutian; Beiping: Dai Zheyi, Yang Zonglian; Zhenjiang: Yang Yuli, Yang Dahui; Changzhou: Jiang Yuhuan, Jia Junhe; Wuxi: Cha Songnian; Suzhou: Chen Zaiwen, Wei Desen; Kaifeng: Qiao Wenhuan, Zhang Guangdai; Daokou: Qiao Wenhuan; Xinxiang: Zhang Guangdai; Anyang: Qiao Wenhuan; Zhengzhou: Tian Jinglian; Luoyang: Han Zhongkui; Huaining: Zhang Yuren; Wuhu: Du Weixuan; Xuzhou: Jiang Zhenggui; Hangzhou: Chen Shigao, Shen Tiansheng; Wenzhou: Chen Shigao; Yin County: Shen Tiansheng; Shaoxing: Shen Tiansheng; Jinan: Huang Zhaoguang, Wu Xingchang; Yantai: Chen Changrong; Qingdao: Yu Xiuchang; Tianjin: Gao Yibang, Zhou Bingwen; Shantou: Xiao Shizhao, Sun Dakun; Nanjing: Wang Xingcang, Kong Fanzao; Yunnan: Wu Tinglun; Nanning: Xu Ziqin, Chen Jinbao; Guangzhou: Zhu Xuefan, Shi Suige, Ge Lianfang, Huang Baokun; Zhangjiakou: Cao Jiaxiu; Liaoning: Cheng Zuoqing; Wuzhou: Li Daming; Guilin: Li Daming; Nanchang: Wan Liangxun; Jiujiang: Yao Gengyang; Fuzhou: Chen Hailan, Chen Danian; Xiamen: Chen Zhang; Bengbu: Li Heqing; Jiangdu: Jiang Hanbo, Song Jilong; Shanghai: Qi Jiamou, Wang Kai.

Local Communications

Songjiang 75

Tax Police Training Institute Continues to Recruit Students: The Tax Police Officer Training Institute of the Salt Affairs Inspection General Office of the Ministry of Finance has been stationed at the gunpowder depot in Songjiang since its establishment to implement training. The head of the institute, Yao Guanshun, is a graduate of the US Army School with excellent academic qualifications and was valued by the late Premier. The instructors at all levels are also US graduates. The second phase of students will hold a graduation ceremony at the end of July, and the third phase will continue to recruit in early August to continue training. These students must be recommended by the salt affairs agency, be at least 21 years old and no more than 28 years old, be of good character and sound physique, and have received secondary education. They must submit a four-and-a-half-inch half-length photo, find a guarantor, and fill out a volunteer form, and the recommending agency must affix a seal to comply with the procedures.

A Thief Escapes After Contracting an Epidemic Disease: Wang Gengsheng, a thief who was not yet sentenced by the County Court, suddenly contracted an epidemic disease in the detention center. The warden, Hu Yaomei, immediately asked a doctor from Songjiang Hospital to treat him. The hospital was not equipped with saline injections, so he had to be transferred to the epidemic hospital. The warden, being serious about human life and preventing infection, immediately sent the prisoner to the Epidemic Hospital of the Red Cross branch for treatment. After the doctor diagnosed him and injected saline, the illness was greatly reduced, but the prisoner took advantage of the guards Zhang Yinqiu's unpreparedness to climb over the back wall while ill and escape. After the guards realized this, they urgently telegraphed the warden, reporting that they had been unable to track him down. It is learned that Warden Hu has not only reported this to the County Court but has also written to the County Public Security Bureau requesting a thorough investigation. The guard on duty has also been investigated by the Procuratorate.

Silk and Cloth Industry Investigates Enemy Goods: Since last year, under the guidance of the Anti-Japanese Association, the silk and cloth industry in this city has registered enemy goods, but they have not been imported again. Recently, there have been peddlers selling printed foreign cloth at reduced prices. After investigation by the industry, it was found that they were all enemy goods. After repeated negotiations, the peddlers voluntarily wrote a letter of repentance and promised not to sell them again. Unexpectedly, before a month had passed, the peddlers relapsed. Therefore, the silk and cloth industry convened a temporary meeting yesterday and decided to elect ten investigators to carry badges and cooperate with personnel sent by the Anti-Japanese Association to be responsible for the investigation in order to rectify the situation. In order to facilitate the execution of their duties, they have submitted a request to the party and government agencies to order them to protect them. The County Government immediately ordered the Public Security Bureau to provide effective protection.

Chongming 76

Discussing the Issue of Chongming and Qidong Joining Governance: Since Chongming and Qidong separated in the 16th year of the Republic of China, local funding has been greatly affected, and all undertakings have been difficult to promote. Disputes between tenants and landlords have repeatedly occurred on both sides (Note: Qidong is the former outer sand of Chongming). Local people have repeatedly petitioned the province to request joint governance, but there has been no appropriate resolution to date. The County Government of this county received an order from the province ordering the county to convene local people to discuss the advantages and disadvantages of the separation and merger of Chongming and Qidong. After receiving the order, the County Government convened a temporary administrative meeting of the entire county in the County Government yesterday. County Magistrate Shen chaired the meeting, and the principles discussed were as follows: (1) The truth and causes of the disputes after the separation of Chongming and Qidong; (2) The advantages and disadvantages of separation and merger. The results of the discussion will be listed with reasons and submitted to the province for review and decision.

Suzhou 77

Arranging Transportation Matters on the Two Railways: Zheng Baozhao, Director of the Transportation Department of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Bureaus, has begun preparations to take charge of railway transportation in accordance with the order of the Ministry. He has repeatedly convened meetings. The plans and methods for responsible transportation on the railway have been largely determined. It is planned to add padlocks and other applied objects such as coarse cloth, hemp rope, bamboo chips, and bamboo buckets. In addition, each station has been notified to quickly repair damaged freight cars and to declare the termination of the lease of each station's freight warehouses by the various transportation companies so that they can be taken back for their own use after the implementation of responsible railway transportation. The implementation date should not be far off.

Wujiang 78

Provincial Security Committee Inspectors Arrive in Jiang: Shen Peng, an inspector of the Provincial Security Committee, arrived in Jiang from the province to inspect the local security corps. It is determined to go to the Tongzhuan area on the 24th, and then to the Li and Lu areas on the 25th, and then to Sheng, Zhen, Yan, and Pinghu, etc.

Results of the County Executive and Supervisory Committee Elections: As a result of the election of the Executive and Supervisory Committees at the 11th Congress of the County Party Department, Xu Yinshi, Jin Weiquan, and Ling Xinzi were elected as Executive Committee members, Xu Renzhi and Pan Xiangjun were elected as Alternate Executive Committee members, Yang Zichun was elected as a Supervisory Committee member, and Qian Xigu was elected as an Alternate Supervisory Committee member.

Wuxi 79

Organizing a Special Epidemic Branch Hospital to Accommodate Sick Inmates: Since the beginning of summer in this county, the weather has been increasingly hot and humid, leading to rampant and widespread epidemics in urban and rural areas. Hospitals are overwhelmed with patients. Several inmates in the county jail, county government prison, prison outposts, and detention centers are dying daily from the epidemic. County Magistrate Chen, recognizing this urgent situation, besides establishing a special epidemic hospital at the Liu Gong Ancestral Hall in Xidun for initial treatment, convened the fourth joint prison meeting the other day. Attendees included committee members Hua Pu, Qian Zhongliang, Zhang Ruiqiang, Zhou Erkai, Yao Dixin, and Wang Li, a total of six people. The meeting was chaired by Chen Chuande. Discussion items included: (1) Regarding the proposal of how to prevent and treat inmates who suddenly fall ill with heatstroke due to the extreme heat and overcrowding, which makes timely treatment difficult, it was resolved to have Hua Pu find a suitable temple to organize a temporary special epidemic branch hospital to accommodate sick inmates for treatment. The expenses will initially be covered by donations from the committee members (an immediate donation of 75 yuan for medical expenses was made by the committee members). (2) Regarding the proposal of how to raise approximately one thousand silver dollars needed for additional prison expenses, which are especially tight, it was resolved to have the association print donation booklets and send them to committee members to solicit donations within a specified timeframe.

A shocking tale of a local ruffian cruelly murdering his own daughter: Tao Kunquan, a well-known local ruffian in Tu 551 of Tengchang Township, Eleventh District (Beixia Township) of this county, is by nature violent and domineering. The villagers fear him like a tiger. Last year, Tao was arrested and sent to the county court for trial. After his release upon completion of his sentence, he did not mend his ways. He began an illicit relationship with Jin, the wife of a villager surnamed Tao, living together as if they were husband and wife, completely neglecting his legal wife, Mao. Mao's daughter, Guiying, who is twelve years old, was abused by the concubine, Jin. Kunquan not only did not stop her, but also joined in the beatings and inflicted various cruel tortures. A week ago, Guiying was severely beaten by Jin and deprived of food and drink. By the day before yesterday, she was on the verge of death. Not satisfied, Jin and Kunquan dragged the girl to the open space in front of their house, tied her with iron bars on her back, and stretched her arms up, exposing her to the scorching sun all day. Around 10:00 PM, Guiying died from her injuries. After hearing this news, Bao Rongqing, the Tu head, reported it to the county court yesterday because the case involved a human life, which he could not conceal. He requested an investigation to verify the facts for further action.

Investigation of Rice Milling Factory's Adulteration of Rice with Stone Powder: Citizens Hu Jia and others reported that a rice milling factory was adulterating rice with stone powder after milling it to increase profits, harming the people. Citing the ban from last year's Executive Yuan, they petitioned the central and provincial authorities for a crackdown. The rice milling industry claimed that Hu and others had ulterior motives, fabricating claims to disrupt business. They petitioned the Ministry of Industry to send personnel to conduct an on-site investigation to clarify the truth. Minister Chen, upon receiving the petition, dispatched Wang Zhen, a technical specialist from the Central Industrial Testing Laboratory, and technician Yu Renhan to Wuxi the other day to conduct an on-site investigation. They met several times with representatives from the county government, chamber of commerce, and the rice milling industry association. On the 22nd, they invited representatives from the county party headquarters, county government, chamber of commerce, and rice and bean industry association to conduct a joint test at the Dexin Rice Mill. They tested both indica and japonica rice, using five, four, three, two, and one jin of powder per shi, as well as rice milled without powder. The representatives participated in the tests, which took an entire day to complete. The results showed that milling rice with five jin of powder per shi yielded eight dou four sheng seven he, and four, four jin yielded eight dou four sheng three he, and one jin yielded eight dou one sheng six he, while milling without powder yielded seven dou six sheng five he. A table was created showing capacity, weight and all representatives signed and sealed to distribute to all parties. Departments Commissioners Wang and Yu returned to Beijing immediately to report back.

Zhenjiang 80

County Party and Government Talk Session: The County Rectification Committee held its fifteenth party and government talk session at 8:00 AM yesterday in the committee's conference room. Discussion items included: (1) The county government's proposal regarding rent reduction for local houses, which was previously resolved at the tenth session of this committee to implement through public notice, is now subject to reconsideration due to a petition from citizen Yu Yin-zeng and others requesting the restoration of the original rent. It was decided that the county government and the provincial Public Security Bureau will jointly issue a notice restoring the original rent from September 1st of this year. (2) The County Rectification Committee's proposal to organize a local committee to abolish silver currency with images of Two Seven Treasures (Erzhibao), so that this can be implemented at an early date, was approved. The committee members will be appointed by the county government and the county party headquarters, selecting fifteen people from party and government agencies and local experts to jointly organize the committee.

A Young Woman Who Failed an Entrance Exam Jumps into the River: Yesterday afternoon, the ferry of Zhenyang Auto Company, heading to Liuyi, reached Taigu Lidang when a young woman, approximately eighteen or nineteen years old, suddenly jumped into the river. The ship's steward noticed this and immediately informed the captain, who stopped the ship. He threw lifebuoys and called for boatmen to rescue her. A boatman jumped into the river and rescued the woman. After receiving emergency treatment, she regained consciousness. When asked her name, she replied that her surname was Tang, her given name Feng, and that she was from Yangzhou. She had come to Zhenjiang to take a middle school entrance exam, but failed. Fearing being ridiculed upon returning to Yangzhou, she briefly lost her senses and jumped into the river. After being rescued, Tang was sent back to the Zhenjiang shore on the original ferry and then taken to the Fifth Precinct by the auto company. The precinct then sent the girl to the Sino-Western Hotel for temporary lodging. Later, the girl said that she had a cousin, surnamed Liu, who lived on Yantou Street in the city. Police were sent to Liu's residence to report the situation, and Liu took her back.

Yangzhou 81

Inspection of the Body of Jiao Fan-hua: The case of Jiao Tingfa, a villager from the Hongqiao area under this county, who beat his son, Jiao Fan-hua, to death and bribed village guard Wang Yu to bury the body, was discovered by the local Public Security Second Precinct. Jiao and Wang were arrested and sent to the court for investigation. It is now known that Fan-hua's body was placed in a coffin and taken to the Zhizhu Temple outside Quekou City. This morning (the 23rd) at 4:00 AM, Prosecutor Meng Zhou, along with an coroner, went to the temple to conduct an inspection. The village guard and others opened the coffin, revealing a severely decomposed body emitting a foul odor. After removing the decayed flesh, the coroner determined that the bones showed signs of strangulation. The prosecutor ordered the bones to be placed back in the coffin, sealed with an official seal, and handed over to the village guard for burial, pending further investigation and prosecution.

Gaoyou 82

Construction of a School Building Causes Dispute: The Songjiaqiao Elementary School in the Eleventh District of this county was originally located in the Gongji Hall for over a decade. Last year, during a flood, the school building was completely destroyed. The county government ordered Yang Shishan, the education committee member of the Fifth School District, to be responsible for the construction. Yang hired workers to begin construction on the 16th of this month. Unexpectedly, Feng Zhaofu, a resident of Jiangdu County, came to stop the construction, claiming that the land was inherited from his ancestors. Yang sent a letter to the police team stationed in the town, requesting them to send two soldiers to maintain order. Feng then led a group of people to disarm the soldiers. One soldier was captured. Yang and Shao Hanqin, a special agent of the police team stationed in the town, have come to the city to report to the county government. After receiving the report, County Magistrate Li immediately wrote to the Jiangdu County government to arrest and interrogate Feng Zhaofu.

Nantong 83

Fishery Protection Team Sets Sail to Suppress Bandits: Recently, sea bandits have resurfaced and gathered in the coastal areas of Nantong, Rugao, Haimen, and Qidong, causing significant disturbance. The Jiangsu-Zhejiang Maritime Fishery Administration has dispatched Li Liewu, the captain of the Fishery Protection Team, to lead a team from Lusi to suppress the bandits.

County Government Mortgages to Raise Funds for Dredging: The provincial government issued 52,500 yuan in public works mortgage bonds, instructing the county to use them to cover the Nantong road construction land tax. The county government, however, used those funds to fund the Canal Dredging expense. As the funds have already been designated for dredging, the Jiangbei Canal Project Rehabilitation Committee has repeatedly urged the release of the funds, but little remains. On the 23rd, the county government mortgaged the bonds to various banks, promising to prioritize repayment with this year's road construction land tax revenue.

Hefei 84

Liang Guanying's Troops and Zheng's Brigade Arrive in Hefei: All of Liang Guanying's troops of the Twenty-Fifth Route Army have been transferred to Hefei to concentrate on suppressing the Red Bandits. The Seventeenth Regiment of the Independent Fifth Brigade under Zheng Tingzhen arrived in Hefei from Dingyuan, on the seventeenth evening, and one two regiments stationed inside and outside of the east gate and the third regiment stationed outside the north gate. Brigade Commander Zheng also arrived in Hefei and established the brigade headquarters at Mingjiao Temple. Liang Guanying will also arrive in Hefei soon.

Over Two Thousand Taels of Opium Burned: The county government seized over 2,300 taels of opium in the east and west gates the other day. Yesterday, representatives from various public organizations and the county party headquarters supervised the burning of the opium next to the county government wall.

Shengxian 85

Mountain Factory Households Relocate En Masse: The areas of Yangdakeng, Kaokengwan, Xikengwan, Yangchangwan, Baichai, etc., near Qiancun in western Shengxian, are known to be areas where bandits frequently appear. In order to thoroughly eliminate the bandits, the authorities have ordered the mountain factory households to relocate by a set deadline. It is reported that these mountain factory households have been moving their furniture and belongings en masse. It is also heard that Qiancun, being in a strategically important location, requires a military presence. A security team will be transferred to defend the location.

Notorious Bandit Zhang Wenkang Apprehended: Zhang Wenkang and Zhang Zhiqi, notorious bandits from western Shengxian, conspired to kidnap Yu Ziqing, the owner of a large rubber factory who had just returned from Shanghai, in Zhujiaqiao, Qingshuipu, Zhenhai. On the evening of the 16th of this month, they gathered seven or eight bandits and went to the home of Zhu Shenshui, where Yu was staying. They tied up Zhu and forced him to point out Yu's location. A long-term worker cried out for help and was shot dead by the bandits. The neighboring villagers heard the sound and beat gongs to alert the area, deterring the bandits, who fled along the river. Chen Juzheng, the detective chief of the Sixth Regiment of the Security Team, happened to be patrolling nearby and bravely went forward to pursue them, capturing the bandit leader Zhang Wenkang on the spot and seizing a bandit gun. The remaining bandits fled in disarray. After Chen's team brought the bandit back for interrogation, the criminal confessed without hesitation. It is heard that he has been sent to the regimental headquarters for further questioning.

Xiaoshan 86

People Are Poor and Exhausted, Please Exempt Us from Harsh Taxes: Xiaoshan's eastern townships are silk-producing areas. This year, the silkworm season was disastrous, and the silkworm cocoons failed. The rural economy is in dire straits. In addition, the harvest of sandy soil cotton and soybeans has been reduced due to prolonged moldy rain. Lately, cries of hardship are heard everywhere, and the people are in a difficult situation. Therefore, they can only request exemption from various local donations. It is heard that most people cannot afford the self-government household donations collected by the township offices in the townships. After the establishment of the township offices, they are only focused on collecting donations from each household and provide no benefit to self-government. Moreover, the township chiefs collude with each other to oppress the people, which greatly violates Sun Yat-sen's teachings of rescuing and aiding the people. Currently, the people of various townships, unable to bear this harsh taxation, have sent representatives to the provincial government to petition for an immediate exemption to sustain the people's livelihoods.

Sinking of a Xiaolin Ferry Boat, Loss Compensation: The night ferry boat from Xiaoshan to Linpu sank on the night of the 17th at Banjiangchen due to the cargo being overloaded. The cargo was full of white rice, sesame cakes, tung oil, and cigarettes, worth about 3,500 yuan. The boatman, Wang Fulin, wrote to the county chamber of commerce, requesting them to ask the merchants for reduced compensation for the losses. The cargo was 300 dan of white rice and 200 dan of sesame cakes belonging to Zhou Deyu and Shengyuan. Yesterday, the chamber of commerce summoned the directors of various businesses to hold a meeting to discuss solutions. In addition to the losses from salvaging and selling the goods at reduced prices, the boat owner will pay 350 yuan in full compensation and the rest of the loss will be accepted as bad luck by each business.

Nine Criminals Granted Amnesty: Since the central government promulgated the amnesty ordinance, the county high court has successively reviewed cases and Chief Prosecutor Zheng has approved those who meet the amnesty ordinance to be pardoned. The Xiaoshan County Court Prosecutor's Office has prepared to interrogate and pardon nine criminals, including Xu Zhou, who meet the amnesty ordinance, in order to make the great occasion known.

Important Education News

National Normal University Opposes Stopping Admissions 87

Beiping, 24th – Li Zheng stated that National Normal University is a university that cultivates middle school teachers for the entire country. The Ministry of Education's order to stop admissions prompted our school to request that they consider the special circumstances of National Normal University and approve the continuation of admissions as usual. The joint meeting of all classes in the English Department of the school issued an emergency declaration on the 24th, opposing the suspension of admissions and vowing to save National Normal University. Graduating students also posted notices explaining the reasons for opposing the Ministry of Education's suspension of admissions. The Beiping University Council will convene an emergency meeting within the next few days to discuss steps to oppose the suspension of admissions and decided to convene a representative assembly. If necessary, representatives will be sent to Beijing to petition. The Great Alliance of Primary, Secondary, and Higher Education Institutions sent a telegram to Zhu Jiahua on the 24th, questioning the reasons for the order to suspend admissions and vowing to oppose it to the death on behalf of 150,000 youths.

Jinan University Alumni Association Asks the Ministry of Education Not to Abolish the Law and Education Schools of the Alma Mater 88

The Shanghai Jinan University Alumni Association held its first executive committee meeting the other day at the China News Agency. Wang Weikai, Wei Xinghua, Chen Xiwu, Cai Guoping, Jiang Shanjing, Zhu Chengxun, Zhou Lin, Ping Zuren, and Long Ziqiang (Chen acting), Yang Shuchun) Wang acting chairman Wang Weimin, recorded by Chen Xiwu, resolved: (1) Immediately telegraph the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Education to request the protection of overseas Chinese education, that is, to withdraw the order to abolish the law school and the education school of the alma mater. (2) Immediately telegraph the alumni associations and groups overseas to request unanimous assistance. (3) Contact alumni associations and on-campus students, faculty, and staff in various places to jointly carry out the school protection movement. (4) Immediately telegraph the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission and various overseas Chinese affairs agencies to request the protection of overseas Chinese universities and forward to the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Education to withdraw the order to abolish the two schools of the alma mater. (5) Prepare to establish a club in Shanghai. (6) Investigate the current situation of alumni and allocate the duties of the executive committee members (Standing Committee) Wang Weimin, Jiang Shanjing, Ping Zuren, (Accountant) Zhou Lin, Jiang Shanjing, (Documentary) Wei Xinghua, Wang Weimin, (Interpersonal) Cai Guoping, Yang Shuchun, (Organization) Xu Fu, Ping Zuren, (Publishing) Chen Xiwu, Zhu Chengxun, (General Affairs) Long Ziqiang

Yang Shuchun, an executive committee member of the Shanghai Alumni Association of National Jinan University, has a very busy law practice, and he still needs to study for at least four hours a day. Thus, it is very difficult for him to hold a position on the executive committee. The other day, he formally submitted his resignation, which was not passed. It is heard that Mr. Yang has prepared a letter to firmly resign from each of the alumni and that he will not be responsible for anything from now on.

Zhu Jia-hua's Explanation Regarding the Current Government's University Consolidation Measures 89

Regarding the Merger of the Law and Education Colleges of Jinan University and the Suspension of Enrollment at the Women's College of Arts and Sciences and the Normal College of Peking University

Recently, Minister of Education Zhu Jia-hua gave an explanation regarding the merger of the Law and Education Colleges of Jinan University in Shanghai and the suspension of enrollment at the Women's College of Arts and Sciences, the Law College, and the Normal College of Peking University.

He stated, in brief, that in recent months, people in the national education sector, feeling the urgency of the national crisis, believe that education is the foundation of a nation. Although it is closely related to politics and economics and interacts with them, it cannot be separated. However, even in terms of education itself, the unsatisfactory state of education is an undeniable fact. People often express great opinions and seek reforms with admirable enthusiasm and insightful views. Summarizing opinions from various parties, the focus of discussion is that higher education should aim for enrichment rather than extravagance. It must raise the level of academic research and pay attention to the cultivation of practical talents, valuing quality over quantity. Secondary education should be closely aligned with social needs and provide relief for the national economy. It is believed that the proliferation of ordinary secondary schools is excessive and that vocational education should be expanded and improved to truly increase the productive capacity of society. Primary and social education should respond to the current environment and ensure that out-of-school children receive the necessary education in the shortest possible time. At the same time, efforts must be made to eliminate adult illiteracy. These opinions have become a unified call throughout the country. It is generally believed that education must break away from the traditional concept of cultivating scholar-officials and strive to meet the practical needs of the nation and society and the meaning of modern times. The Ministry itself, since the National Education Conference held in the nineteenth year, resolved to improve the national education program and also planned and compiled it accordingly. Recently, in light of the facts of recent years, the Ministry is also carefully studying and planning successively. However, this matter is of great importance and must be carefully and thoroughly planned. It is hoped that it can be brought to the public for discussion in the near future.

Now, only in terms of national and provincial universities and independent colleges, the poor performance of graduates, the low level of equipment, and the lack of academic competition are almost universal phenomena. However, what is most regrettable is the lack of direction and planning in running schools. Establishing universities and departments often ignores the objective environment and their basic foundations. They imitate each other, admire vanity, and engage in extravagance and specialization in superficiality. Setting courses and opening lectures often neglects the study of basic subjects and the reality of various disciplines, resulting in superficiality and complexity without regard for the system. These two factors cause the first problem: in the same area, universities established by the same government have overlapping departments. In terms of equipment, they all lack it. In terms of professors and teaching materials, they are often the same people and the same things. On the other hand, in a smaller city, the various colleges of liberal arts that do not require huge equipment costs strive to have everything. Even in an engineering college that requires huge equipment costs, departments of civil engineering, electrical engineering, mechanical engineering, chemistry, architecture, mining, and metallurgy must be complete, regardless of the equipment capacity or local needs. The second problem is that materials that can be encompassed in one subject of study are deliberately fragmented. Basic subjects are neglected, and novelty is pursued. Ordinary physics is not yet understood, but the theory of relativity must be studied. The history of economic thought is not systematically discussed, but the theories of figures such as Marx must be opened as a separate course. Based on these two factors, the extravagance, superficiality, complexity, and fundamental nature of the university are already like this, and scholars can understand the consequences. Given China's current human and financial resources, even if the government concentrates its efforts on running three or five universities, it is still worried that it will not be enough. Since the tenth year of the Republic, only the high-sounding slogans of the university reform movement have been seen, and the substantial progress of universities has been rarely seen. Those who talk about university education often blame the poor politics, the lack of funds, and the lack of career paths for graduates. Their words are indeed true. However, upon considering the situation, this is only a one-sided observation. Therefore, the rationalization, consolidation, and enrichment of universities is a very urgent and important issue. However, this matter is very complex and requires thorough discussion to obtain a proper and appropriate plan. Without the thorough understanding and joint efforts of those engaged in university education, it is not possible to improve academics. Academics are public property, and universities are institutions for academic research. They should not be privately owned or restricted by any person, history, or purpose other than academics. The era of truth and the future of culture are constantly illuminating us. The various unsatisfactory states of current university education are not entirely avoidable by any one school, nor should any one person be held responsible. Joint efforts must be made to continuously consolidate and enrich them in order to achieve a rational solution.

As for the government's decision to merge the Law College and the Education College of Jinan University and to suspend enrollment this year at the Women's College of Arts and Sciences, the Law College, and the Normal College of Peking University, it is not any strange fact, but merely one step in the consolidation work. The purpose of establishing Jinan University was to educate the children of overseas Chinese. The government, mindful of their virtuous labor, specially established this school. Some people believe that the children of overseas Chinese only need to set up separate primary and secondary schools to provide special education, and that there is no need to isolate them in universities. They should be integrated with domestic youth to learn more about the culture and customs of the motherland. In fact, most of the children of overseas Chinese who return to the country are educated in universities other than Jinan. Furthermore, more than half of the current students at Jinan are not children of overseas Chinese. This is another argument. Now, only in terms of merging the Law College and the Education College of the school, the school unfortunately suffered damage from the Japanese aggression. Although the government decided to hand over the disaster-stricken schools in Shanghai to the Post-War Relief Committee for overall relief, it is observed that the relief efforts of the committee may be difficult to compensate for the losses in a short period of time. Therefore, the school must adopt a policy of austerity and concentration in order to ensure that the effectiveness of education is not reduced. President Zheng has also made plans for the merger of academic departments. Shanghai is only seven hours away from Nanjing, where the national government is located and where political implementation originates. Many scholars of law and politics are also gathered in this place. Therefore, it is ordered to abolish the Law College and transfer the existing students to National Central University. As for the renaming of the Education College to the Department of Education, it is like the merger of the four departments of the Education College of Central University into one department. Renaming a college to a department does not mean disrespecting the study of education. University students studying education to prepare for teaching is excellent, and it is especially necessary for overseas Chinese youth. However, establishing a special college to study education subjects means that, on the one hand, there is a lack of research in basic arts and sciences subjects. How can one be a teacher without the study of other subjects besides education? On the other hand, if students specializing in education are allowed, where will they find opportunities for educational administration after graduation? In short, the purpose of Jinan University, in addition to academic research, is in fact to train teachers and develop business talents. In this regard, it is appropriate to retain the College of Arts, the College of Sciences, the College of Commerce, and the primary and secondary schools specially established for overseas Chinese children. Furthermore, using the funds from the original Law College and Education College to compensate for the disaster and enrich the content of the College of Arts, the College of Sciences, the College of Commerce, and the primary and secondary schools, the future is very promising.

Furthermore, Peking University has seven colleges with approximately 2,600 students. The College of Art and the College of Russian Language and Politics were ordered by the Ministry to stop enrollment in the nineteenth year and were gradually closed. Some people advocate that the Women's College of Arts and Sciences should be renamed a women's university to foster talent, taking into account family customs and the special strengths of women. Others believe that men and women are already admitted to all universities and colleges, and there is no need to establish any special university or college. This issue remains to be studied. Although both Peking University and Tsinghua University have established Law Colleges, some believe that the research in the Law Colleges of these two schools is focused on theoretical aspects, while the Law College of Peking University should focus on practical aspects in the future to cultivate legal talents for application. This is also an issue that remains to be studied. The Normal University has approximately 1,600 students and aims to train secondary school teachers. However, according to the current content, it is no different from ordinary universities and suffers from the problem of a mismatch between name and reality. Recently, some people have advocated that the Normal University should only admit university graduates who are interested in secondary school education to study education for one year. Others have advocated maintaining the current system and tailoring the curriculum to meet the purpose of serving as teachers. These issues cannot be easily decided. In general, the overlapping of departments in national universities in the area of Peking is obvious. The government is also extremely concerned about the inadequacy of equipment in Peking University and the Normal University, especially the unfortunate fire that occurred in the physics laboratory of the Normal University last year. In recent years, the two schools have repeatedly experienced unrest, and the complexity of the content has made those who run the schools feel deeply troubled. The government's decision to suspend enrollment at the Normal University and the Women's College of Arts and Sciences affiliated with Peking University was originally intended to facilitate the consolidation and improvement of the schools and colleges.

The enrollment of schools is originally a kind of educational plan. On the one hand, it must consider the needs of society, and on the other hand, the school must consider its own ease of educational effectiveness. The current common practice of schools is that each college and department has no choice, how can it be good? The original students of the Normal University and the Law College and the Women's College of Arts and Sciences of Peking University are already quite numerous, and there is also an oversupply of this kind of talent in society for a while, so suspending the recruitment of new students is a matter that should be done. One must know that enrollment is one plan of running a school. Whether a school or college should recruit new students and how many should be recruited should have a provision. The government's decision this time is not intended to be unfair. For example, the approval of the College of Engineering, the College of Agriculture, and the College of Medicine of Peking University to recruit students does not mean that the performance of these three colleges is better than other colleges. This is because there are not many such colleges in Peking, and the country is in great need of construction talents, and consideration must be given to the education of young people from all over the country.

In short, the government's consolidation measures for Central University, Labor University, Qingdao University, Jinan University, Peking University, and the Normal University have all been carefully decided after a very long period of discussion. All the measures for consolidation, reorganization, and suspension of enrollment seem to be negative actions on the surface. Those who have ill intentions may even criticize them as destroying existing education. In fact, the positive significance is extremely profound. Everything is for the convenience of the students' own studies and the convenience of those who are enthusiastic about running schools. Plans are made with the most careful consideration. Strict consolidation measures will also be adopted for all private universities in the future, so that young people throughout the country can have a genuine venue to pursue their studies and be useful to the country. The government is concerned about the national crisis and expects the universities to make a great contribution to the country. The expressions of people in the society in recent months also share this view. In short, the consolidation of universities is not a matter of one time, but requires long-term efforts, and it cannot be achieved by the government alone. It is hoped that those engaged in university education will work together to promote progress. Now that the government is in financial difficulties, it is striving to fully issue the funds for national universities and colleges from this month onwards to avoid reductions. Everyone sees the hard work involved. How will the performance of the universities be next year? It depends on our efforts today. The Ministry is responsible for education and is extremely willing to accept opinions from all parties on how to improve education in the future in order to achieve perfection. At the same time, for any decision of the government, it can only be implemented with sincerity and courage, without fear of labor or resentment.

New Developments at Suzhou Agricultural School 90

Suzhou Agricultural School has been determined to reform in recent years, with remarkable achievements. Liao Jianan, the principal of the school, has made every effort in planning and operation. A reorganization plan has been set since the 21st academic year and will be carried out gradually to promote the innovation of vocational education. Many faculty and staff have also been hired, such as Huang Gutong, the director of the Department of Sociology of the College of Agriculture of Zhejiang University, Yu Yunsheng, a professor at Zhejiang University, Tang Quansheng, the former president of Huaiyin Agricultural School, Zhang Sizhi, a lecturer at Central University, Zeng Hanqing, the former director of the Zhejiang Sericulture Experiment Station, and horticultural expert Li Menglong, and economic expert Huang Zixiong, who have all been appointed to teaching positions.

Grass Court Tennis Group A Championship: China and Japan Compete for the Title 93

Looking Forward to Wednesday's Decisive Battle

The Shanghai Grass Court Tennis Group A Championship has now become a contest between China and Japan. Based on recent results and the strength of both sides, Japan has taken a superior position. If China can display a spirit of dauntlessness and work hard to compete, then this glimmer of hope is not impossible to achieve the final victory. The warriors who bear the name of China should know the importance of their responsibilities. In the past six matches between the Chinese and Japanese teams, China won 66 sets and lost 24 sets, while Japan won 73 sets and lost 17 sets. In Wednesday's match, if China can win 11 to 4, then each side will have won 77 sets, resulting in a tie. If there is an even better result, such as 12 to 3, then China can take the lead. On the contrary, Japan only needs to win 5 sets to retain the title. The difficulty of the facts for both sides is like this, and the future result may not be what China hopes for.

Baseball Practice Match: China Loses to Mailing 94

China Lacks Training and Has Unfamiliar Skills

Mailing B Wins 8 to 2

The Chinese baseball team played a practice match against Mailing B yesterday at the Chinese baseball field. This was the Chinese team's debut since its formation. They lost due to seven errors. As a result, Mailing got ten hits and won 8 to 2. About 500 or 600 people watched, and the atmosphere was quite enthusiastic. China's defeat was due to a lack of training, unfamiliar skills, and a disorganized lineup that was difficult to control. However, the talent is quite average, and if they can be given time to train, the future is very promising. The following is a record of yesterday's events.

Pitcher Wei Has Some Skill 95

Chinese pitcher Wei Zongwei was formerly a pitcher for the Yokohama Chinese Baseball Association and is a second-class player in the Japanese overseas Chinese community (the first-class pitcher in the Japanese overseas Chinese community is Liu Sezhang, who is currently studying at Hosei University and has not yet enlisted). Yesterday, he struck out (three hits) eight times, matching Mailing's pitch Locke Zasa (four ball counts). Wei only gave up twice, while Mailing's pitch gave up six times. It is said that Wei's performance yesterday did not seem to be at its best.

The Liang Brothers' Skills Are Outstanding 96

Catchers Zhang Guoxun and Liu Dacheng were quite calm, but they were inevitably unfamiliar due to a lack of practice. First baseman Liang Fuchu is old but strong and worthy of his reputation as a general. He is in charge of issuing orders and has experience in commanding the line. Liang Chengshan, who is stationed at second base, is quick and nimble, has clever actions, and has a unique skill in stealing bases. The rest of the players are also of average quality. However, their batting skills are still lacking.

Mailing Scores Two Points in the First Three Innings 97

The attack started at 4:20 pm, with Mailing batting first. Both sides were cautious and made no progress. In the second inning, Mailing scored two consecutive hits. Cowbell and Morgan returned to score two points. China attacked hard and Liang Fuchu reached third base. Wei Zongwei also occupied second base, but two people had already been eliminated, and Gu Degang's high ball was struck out, and all previous efforts were in vain. In the third inning, Mailing's Allart had a great opportunity to return to base from third base, but China's tight union kill was luckily not successful. China was still scoreless in this inning.

Mailing Wins Again with Repeated Hits 98

Mailing continued to attack. Fliehmann threw a high ball that flew far into the back of the outfield, and Gu Degang failed to catch it. Then, Cowbell and Morgan each made hits. In addition, Liu Dacheng made a mistake, and the two returned to score two more points. China was still scoreless. At the end of the fourth inning, Mailing won with a score of 4-0. In the upper half of the fifth inning, Mailing's momentum was even stronger, with continuous hits and bases full of power. Fortunately, China worked hard and Wei Zongwei displayed his skills to eliminate Mailing without success. China also did not gain any points.

Zongwei's Hit, Li and Gu Return 99

After Mailing's unsuccessful change of formation in the sixth inning, China worked hard to counterattack. Liu Dacheng got a base on balls, Zhang Zhaoyuan released a hit, and each occupied one base. When Liang Fuchu got to first base, Liu Dacheng was killed at third base. Then, Li Beiliang released a long ball, and Zhang Zhaoyuan rushed back to home base, but Mailing's left fielder had already sent the ball to home base, and Zhang was unfortunately touched out. Fortunately, Wei Zongwei got a hit, and the ball flew far to the right field. Gu Degang replaced Liang Fuchu and ran back to home base, and Li Beiliang also returned, scoring two points. The audience cheered.

Mailing Continued to Score Five Hits 100

In the final seventh inning, China was very depressed. Mailing scored five consecutive hits, and each base was occupied. Enemy Buxel, Simen, Hailang, and Fliehmann returned to score four more points. China persevered and Liang Chengsong stole a base and advanced to third base, hoping to return, but An Lesheng (pinch hitter) was killed because of his risk, and all previous efforts were in vain, which was very regrettable. As a result, China lost 2-8. The game was judged by umpire Carroll and the base umpire was Mullen, and the game ended at 6:10 pm, lasting 1 hour and 50 minutes.
