After the Implementation of the Blockade of the Northeast Post Office 106

A large number of postal personnel were ordered to withdraw and enter the pass The Japanese instigated the puppet state to take over and issue counterfeit new stamps A temporary post office was set up at the Japanese Consulate in this city to send letters Because the Japanese instigated the puppet state to sabotage and harass the Northeast Post Office, the Ministry of Communications ordered the General Post Office to implement the blockade, and ordered all postal personnel in the area to leave the bureau. The details have been recorded in yesterday's newspaper. The news from yesterday is recorded as follows.

Japanese Seize the Eastern Provinces Postal Bureau 107

The Japanese had already established Japanese postal bureaus within the South Manchurian Railway Zone in northeastern China. The area along the South Manchurian Railway was designated as a Japanese postal district. Since the September 18th Incident, the Japanese have been plotting to seize our country's postal affairs, secretly preparing vigorously. However, due to incomplete preparations, they delayed implementation. After our country ordered a blockade and the withdrawal of postal personnel from various districts in the Northeast, the Japanese openly proceeded with the takeover, with everything directed by the Japanese Fujiwara, the head of the puppet state's postal administration. According to sources in the postal circles in this port, the Japanese are gradually taking over various postal bureaus and are expected to complete the takeover within days.

A large number of postal workers are leaving their posts. The northeastern postal districts are divided into two: the Liaoning District and the Jilin-Heilongjiang District. After receiving orders from the General Post Office, they have been withdrawing one after another. Currently, the Liaoning District Postal Director, Italian Bali Di, and the Jilin-Heilongjiang District Postal Director, British Smith, have issued orders to their subordinate postal personnel to leave their posts and return to the interior. As for the lower-level staff, most of them were hired locally after passing examinations, so they remain in place and are not withdrawing. The northeastern postal personnel have telegraphed the Shanghai General Post Office regarding the withdrawal situation.

New Postal Stamps Discovered in the Rebel Areas After the withdrawal of personnel from the Northeastern Postal Bureau, the Japanese incited rebels to take over. The puppet organization is now creating postal stamps, which have been discovered within our borders. The printing and platemaking are entirely handled by the Japanese. The designs are very similar to Chinese postal stamps. The images printed on the stamps include pagodas and portraits of Puyi. The denominations on the stamps include one cent, two cents, four cents, five cents, ten cents, twenty cents, fifty cents, one yuan, two yuan, and many other denominations. Currently, letters within the rebel areas can still be delivered as usual by the puppet state, but letters sent to the interior are blocked by our country's postal authorities and cannot be delivered.

The General Post Office Telegraphs the Ministry of Communications This Port

The General Post Office has been quite busy in recent days with the issue of blockading postal services outside Shanhaiguan, working through the night with lights burning. Yesterday was Sunday, normally a day off, but the bureau still operated as usual. Director Huang telegraphed the Ministry of Communications regarding the situation after the blockade.

Japanese Consulate Establishes Temporary Post Office The Japanese

authorities stationed in Shanghai were greatly alarmed after hearing the news of the blockade of the northeastern postal service. Yesterday morning, they held a meeting to discuss establishing a temporary post office within the Japanese Consulate to collect mail from Japanese residents and transport it to the three northeastern provinces via the Dalian Steamship Company, to mitigate the inconvenience after the blockade.

Continuous Meetings Held by Song Ziwen 108

Discussing the Northeast Customs

and the Abolition of Taels and Currency Reform

According to the Central News Agency, Finance Minister Song Ziwen, after arriving in Shanghai from Nanjing the day before, immediately summoned Chief Inspector of Customs Frederick Maze, Director of Customs Zhang Fuyun, and senior Chinese and foreign personnel from both Customs administrations. They held continuous meetings at the Song residence to discuss how to deal with the rebels seizing Northeast customs duties. At the same time, he summoned Bei Songsun, Li Fusun, and others from the Shanghai banking and financial circles to discuss implementing the abolition of taels and currency reform. Significant progress has been made in both areas.

Northeast Customs Regarding Responding to the Rebels’ Seizure of Customs Duties The Minister of Finance believes that customs revenue from the three northeastern provinces is related to the entire national finances and absolutely cannot allow external interference. Moreover, Northeast customs revenue involves domestic and foreign debt issues. Our country should strive to recover it, and all related countries should pay close attention to it. After days of discussion by Minister Song and others, considerable results have been achieved. At 10:00 AM yesterday, foreign advisors such as Mr. Yang of the Customs were summoned again. Steps have reportedly been formulated regarding the blockade of the Northeast customs and the dismissal of Japanese employees of various customs offices, but they cannot be announced before implementation.

Abolition of Taels and Currency Reform The financial authorities have repeatedly discussed the issue of abolishing taels and reforming the currency with various banking and financial circles and experts in this port to rectify the domestic currency system. During this trip to Shanghai, Song summoned Bei Songsun, Li Fusun, and others from the Shanghai banking and financial circles the night before and discussed the matter in detail for two hours. It is now known that Song is very busy discussing Northeast customs and planning funds for suppressing bandits, so the issue of abolishing taels and currency reform will be temporarily handled by Deputy Minister of Finance Zhang Shouyong in consultation with the Shanghai banking and financial circles. Therefore, Zhang consulted with Hu Mengjia of the Bank of Communications and others on methods yesterday morning at around 10:00 AM.

Suppression of Bandit Funds As a result of the previous discussions between President Wang and Finance Minister Song in Shanghai regarding funds for suppressing bandits, the monthly increase was 1.5 million yuan. Song’s trip to Wuhan to visit Chiang Kai-shek was to report in detail on the progress of planning the funds for suppressing bandits. Therefore, Song’s most important task in coming to Shanghai this time is to plan these funds and the issue of Northeast customs duties. Therefore, he has been meeting with the Shanghai banking and financial circles in recent days, and it is reported that a solution has been largely reached.

Will Go to Kuling According to the Xin Sheng News Agency, Finance Minister Song Ziwen rested at his residence all day yesterday and did not go out. Among those who visited in the morning was Advisor Yang of the Ministry of Finance. It is said that they continued to discuss the blockade of Northeast customs. No guests visited in the afternoon. As for the news that came from the banking circles the day before, claiming that Minister Song would host a banquet for the banking and financial industries last night to continue negotiating on military spending for suppressing bandits and the abolition of taels and currency reform, Xin Sheng News Agency reporters inquired at the Song residence yesterday and were told that this was not the case. It is not clear whether it was a misunderstanding by the banking circles or a temporary suspension. However, according to reliable sources, Minister Song will return to Nanjing this week and then go to Kuling. There are also reports that he will leave today.

Officially Established on August 2nd The Executive Committee Met Yesterday to Discuss the Articles of Association The Shanghai money industry reserve bank, which was resolved to be established by the money industry association and is being actively carried out, is scheduled to be established on August 2nd. The details are as follows: Scheduled Establishment The articles of association of the money industry joint reserve bank were drafted yesterday by Qin Siqing, the secretary-general of the money industry association. The content is very detailed. Qin graduated from a foreign business school, has studied financial theory, and served as the manager of the Hankou Zhongfu Bank for more than ten years. He has rich experience. Since taking office as the secretary-general of the association, he has become particularly familiar with the situation in the money industry. Therefore, he is naturally able to handle all the designs for organizing a joint reserve bank with ease. The reserve bank has now decided to hold a members' representative meeting at the Ningbo Road Money Industry Association at 2:00 PM on August 2nd to formally establish the bank and elect committee members.

Fund Deposited The special property management committee of the money industry association has completely ended and stopped working. All the staff are preparing for the joint reserve bank. As for the reserve amount of the reserve bank, it is stipulated to be more than 30 million yuan. Among them, the value of the property is estimated to be more than 27 million yuan, and the fund of the former property management committee has been transferred. If they can persevere and struggle to the end, the results in the future will be considerable. As for the location of the reserve bank, it will be in a new building next to the Tongyuan Bank on Tianjin Road.

Reviewing the Articles of Association The money industry association held an executive committee meeting at 2:00 PM yesterday. They will be passed at the members' general meeting on August 2nd.

Establishment Mission Xin Sheng News Agency reporters met with Qin Xieqing, the secretary-general of the money industry association, yesterday. According to him, the money industry guild draft houses and yuan-character colleagues have joined the joint reserve bank. The bank was specially established to consolidate the credibility of the entire industry, and its mission is to regulate the financial market and become a permanent organization. The reserve funds paid are: (A) cargo warehouse receipts that can be priced immediately; (B) real estate with a valuation; (C) cash currency or cash notes; (D) existing treasures or existing foreign currency. The committee members will properly evaluate the deposited property, and if the price falls in the future, they must still notify them to replenish it.

Foreign Goods Sold Should Be Labeled with Their Country of Origin 113

So That Customers Can Easily Recognize Them The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Notified Various Industry Associations Yesterday: To The Respected Addressee, On The 22nd Of This Month, We Received A Letter From The China International Trade Association, Stating That Our Country's Industry And Commerce Are Still Nascent, And Domestic Products Are Insufficient To Supply The Needs. It Is Necessary To Transport And Sell Necessary Foreign Goods To Meet Domestic Demand. Moreover, World Transportation Is Becoming More And More Convenient, And International Trade Is Growing. It Is Natural To Exchange What One Has For What One Needs. However, There Are Differences In The Quality Of Imported Goods, And There Are Differences In The Nationalities Of Manufacturers. Merchants Have No Preferences For Good Or Bad In Their Pursuit Of Profit, And Customers Have No General Psychology In Their Selection Of Superior Products. Recently, The Market Is Flooded With Foreign Goods, But The Sellers Do Not Indicate Which Country The Goods Are From Or Which Factory Made Them. Buyers Often Have To Ask, And They Often Fail To Answer Properly, Which Leads To A Loss Of Affection And Damage To Transactions. The Beginning Is Small, But The Impact Is Great. Moreover, The Reason Why Our Country's Industry And Commerce Are Backward Is Not Just One End, But Self-Containment And A Lack Of Progress Are The Most Important Reasons. If Stores And Customers Can Pay Attention To Comparing Various Imported Goods And Study The Advantages Of Each, They Can Also Take This Opportunity To Correct Mistakes, So That The Industrial Sector Can Intend To Improve What They Already Have And Carefully Imitate What They Do Not Have. It Is Not Difficult To Develop Industry, And Leakage Can Be Slightly Blocked. The Fifth Board Of Directors Of Our Association, Based On The Above Reasons, Resolved To Suggest That Your Association Be Requested To Inform Various Industry Associations To Label The Foreign Goods They Sell With Their Country Of Origin Within The Possible Range, So That Customers Can Recognize Them And Provide Reference For Entrepreneurs. We Send This Letter Accordingly, Hoping That You Will Investigate And Handle It And Show Your Public Friendship, Etc. It Is True That The Above-Mentioned Requirement That Stores In Various Industries Should Label The Foreign Goods They Sell With Their Country Of Origin So That Customers Can Easily Recognize Them And Entrepreneurs Can Use Them As A Reference Is Indeed Beneficial To The Domestic Industrial And Commercial Circles. We Send This Letter In Accordance With The Situation Of The Letter, Hoping That Your Association Will Investigate And Advise Your Members To Follow And Implement It Within The Possible Range. This Is What We Expect.

Song Shi, Director of the Shanghai Arsenal, Resigned 115

The Arsenal Affairs Are Temporarily Handled by Liu Shouyu, According to Datong News Agency: The new factory site of the Shanghai Arsenal was previously surveyed and determined to be Xucun, Hangzhou. Later, Hong Zhong, director of the Ordnance Department of the Ministry of War, believed that Hangzhou was not suitable for establishing a factory, so he went to Wuhan to ask Chiang Kai-shek for instructions, advocating moving to Nanjing. Chiang reportedly agreed in person. Now, the order from the Ministry of Military Administration has arrived, ordering the relocation and merger of the medicine manufacturing, gun manufacturing, bullet manufacturing, shell manufacturing, and machine manufacturing factories to Jinling. The Ordnance Department then ordered the factory to expedite the completion of the closure. Song Shi, the director of the factory, had previously submitted his resignation to the Ordnance Department, which is said to have been approved. The arsenal affairs are temporarily handled by Liu Shouyu, director of the Engineering Department. The details are as follows:

Hong Zhong Advocated Moving to Nanjing The new factory site of the Shanghai Arsenal was originally surveyed and determined to be Xucun, 20 miles from Hangzhou. After the new factory site was surveyed, senior officials of the factory convened a work conference and drafted a plan for the construction of the new factory in Xucun, which was submitted to the military department for review. Later, Hong Zhong, director of the Ordnance Department, believed that Hangzhou had a prosperous business and that it was not suitable to build a factory there. Therefore, he personally went to Wuhan to visit Chiang Kai-shek and explained the situation, advocating starting construction in Nanjing. Chiang reportedly nodded in agreement. Hong then returned to Nanjing and telegraphed Hu Sihong, director of the Review and Inspection Department of the Shanghai factory, and Lin Weirong, director of the Bullet Factory, to go to Nanjing. At that time, Hu and others were still unaware that the plan to move to Hangzhou had been changed, so they still carried the previous plan to Nanjing. Later, Director Gang explained that the original plan had been changed and held concrete discussions in the Ordnance Department. Because the Ministry of Military Administration had not yet issued a clear order, Hu and others first returned to Shanghai.

Ordnance Department Ordered the Closure The Ministry of Military Administration considered the relocation of the factory to Nanjing to be feasible, so it has been approved. After receiving the order, the Ordnance Department telegraphed the factory on the 21st to comply. The telegram read, "According to the order of the Ministry, the machines of the gun manufacturing, medicine manufacturing, bullet manufacturing, shell manufacturing, and machine manufacturing factories will be relocated and merged to Jinling. You should comply." On the same day, the factory was also telegraphed to expedite the completion of the closure. The telegram read, "The factory has been ordered by the Ministry to relocate and merge to Jinling. You should expedite the completion of the closure in order to facilitate the relocation. During the closure period, the original employees should continue to serve as before. After the new factory is established, they will be re-evaluated and retained or dismissed. You should announce this to all."

Song Shi Resigned Song Shi, the director of the factory, became very passive after the January 28th Incident and the relocation of the factory's machines to Hangzhou. Therefore, before leaving Shanghai to go to Qingdao to avoid the summer heat, he submitted his resignation to the Ordnance Department and handed over the arsenal affairs to Liu Shouyu, director of the Engineering Department, as his agent. The Ordnance Department is said to have approved Song's resignation, and Liu Shouyu is to temporarily handle the arsenal affairs. Since the closure is imminent, Song has been telegraphed to return to Shanghai to handle the handover. Liu's trip to Nanjing was to request instructions from the Ordnance Department regarding the closure of the factory. It is said that the factory's employees expressed dissatisfaction with the relocation to Nanjing, so they sent Liu as a representative to Nanjing to discuss the matter with the Ordnance Department, which is completely inaccurate.

Artillery Factory Moved to Hanyang The factory originally had seven factories: artillery manufacturing, gun manufacturing, medicine manufacturing, bullet manufacturing, shell manufacturing, machine manufacturing, and steelmaking. After the steelmaking factory was separated by order of the Ordnance Department, there were still six factories left. This time, in addition to the gun manufacturing, medicine manufacturing, bullet manufacturing, shell manufacturing, and machine manufacturing factories, which were ordered to move to Nanjing, the artillery manufacturing factory continues to work as usual because the repair works have not been completed. As soon as the work is completed, the machines of the factory must be merged into Hanyang.

Ma Kui and Others Returned North Yesterday 116

Ma Kui, the son of Ma Zhanshan, the chairman of Heilongjiang Province, Chief of Staff Wang Duo, Commander-in-Chief of the Northeast Volunteer Army Ding Shiqiang, and Zang Qifang and others, who had traveled from overseas and detoured to the south, had been here for more than 20 days. They had contacted the central government in Nanjing and visited Chiang Kai-shek and Zhang Xueliang in Wuhan. After arriving in Shanghai the day before, they had also consulted with various groups in Shanghai. Ministry of Justice Prepares to Revise the Special District Court Agreement 122

To Be Submitted When It Expires in April Next Year

The Most Important Points Are Bailiffs and Prisons

The Shanghai First Special District Local Court Agreement will expire on April 1 next year. The Ministry of Judicial Administration is currently preparing revisions. It is understood that in addition to the Special District, there are also the Higher Court Second Branch of the Public Concession, the Higher Court Third Branch of the French Concession, and the Second Special District Local Court. The agreements of these three courts will also expire at the same time. When the time comes, not only will the First Special District Court Agreement need to be revised, but the agreements of the other three courts will also be revised at the same time. According to a reporter from the New Sound News Agency, the candidates for revising the agreement have not yet been decided, but the scope of the revision includes the following:

(1) Police Power: Currently, the judicial police power of the court is in the hands of foreigners. All arrests, searches, and other matters must be done through foreigners, which is quite inconvenient for command. In the future, when the agreement is revised, this police power will be returned to the jurisdiction of the court, and the police station will be in a supporting position.

(2) Lawyer's Rights: According to Chinese law, foreign lawyers are not allowed to appear in Chinese courts. However, due to the provisions of the agreement, foreign lawyers can appear in court to defend Chinese and foreign cases. After the agreement is revised, the right of foreign lawyers to appear in court will no longer be allowed to exist.

(3) Prison Rights: Currently, the prison laws of the courts, the French Concession Higher Third Branch, and the Second Special District Local Court have been returned to the French authorities when they were taken back. As for the prison rights of the First Special District Court and the Higher Second Branch of the Public Concession (civil case criminals and female prisoners) have already been taken back by our side, so they will also be taken back in the future. Other issues, such as the investigation power of the prosecutor, are also under consideration by the Ministry of Judicial Administration.

Yu Qiaqing Publishes a Talk on Abolishing Taels and Changing to Yuan 124

Recently, the issue of abolishing taels and changing to yuan has received close attention from all sectors. The reporter, considering that Mr. Yu Qiaqing has been in Shanghai for fifty years and is the祭酒 of Shanghai's commerce, specially went to ask for his opinion on this issue. He was pleased to publish the following remarks. Mr. Yu said that the harm of using both taels and yuan and the benefits of abolishing taels and changing to yuan are already known to everyone and do not need to be repeated. I dare to say that all industries in Shanghai will definitely not oppose this move or harbor secret dissent. However, in everything under heaven, there are benefits and harms. People today only know the benefits of abolishing taels and changing to yuan, but they do not consider how to study and eliminate the harms that will arise after abolishing taels and changing to yuan in advance. This is a big mistake. Although the names of silver taels in various places are complex, the value is consistently calculated based on the actual weight throughout the country. Silver yuan, on the other hand, are not. There are dozens of kinds, including British 洋, 本洋, 站人洋, 北洋龙洋, Yuan coins, and Premier coins. This only refers to hard currency. As for paper money, there are countless kinds throughout the country, making it difficult to enumerate them all. If we do not first comprehensively reorganize and start with a thorough reform, but blindly engage in it, how can we achieve results? For example, if a house leaks, someone proposes to replace it with a new one. This is something everyone agrees with, but before moving into the new house, we must study whether the new house is suitable and whether it has any shortcomings. If we rashly demolish the old house and move into the new house, if the new house leaks even worse, or if the sanitation is unsuitable or the architecture is incompatible, wouldn't we be in a dilemma and force the family to spend the night in the open air? Also, we know that to build a mansion, we must first consolidate the foundation. Rectifying hard currency is consolidating the foundation. Therefore, I advocate that before implementing the abolition of taels and changing to yuan, we must first have sufficient arrangements and preparations and must not implement it hastily. In short, the principle of abolishing taels and changing to yuan is absolutely indisputable, but water can help people and also drown them. It depends on the authorities' ability to use it well.

Organizers Exchanged Views Yesterday Afternoon

The Philie Lace Industry Appeals for Exemption from Business Tax 129

Sends a Letter to the Pudong Fellow Townsmen Association for Assistance

The Philie Lace Industry has repeatedly applied to the Ministry for exemption from business tax based on the principles and methods for reducing and exempting business tax decided by the 47th National Affairs Conference, but it has not been approved. Now, in accordance with the Court's decree, it is appealing to the Pudong Fellow Townsmen Association for assistance. The letter says: "We respectfully inform you that Philie lace is a special product of Chuansha and Nanhui in Pudong. It is purely a handicraft industry of poor rural women. Its exquisite products are praised all over the world and are sold from Shanghai to Europe and the United States. Before ten years ago, the output increased year by year. At its peak, the total value reached about 3 million yuan. In the past ten years, due to the manipulation and control of foreign merchants, business has gradually declined. The total value of current sales is only about 1 million yuan. During the former Beijing government, it was approved to exempt from customs export tax and domestic goods tax, so the cost was not increased, and it was barely maintained, providing a livelihood for hundreds of thousands of poor people in Pudong. Unexpectedly, after the implementation of tax cuts, the government changed to collect business tax to compensate. According to the business tax regulations of Jiangsu Province, the lace industry is taxed at 20 per mille of the business turnover. Later, it was reported to the Ministry of Finance for approval to reduce it to 5 per mille. The Provincial Government ordered the county to comply. Under the order of our association, Shanghai lace is taxed because it is a combined business with a wide business scope and large sales volume, and it has been approved to exempt from business tax. Philie lace, on the other hand, is coarser than lace embroidery and has a narrower business scope, but it is taxed at a high rate of business tax, which is contrary to the principle of fair taxation. Therefore, we immediately referred to the Shanghai tax exemption precedent and reported to the Chuansha County Government for forwarding for tax exemption. We were then instructed by the county magistrate to forward the instructions from the Provincial Finance Office, stating that it was not appropriate to refer to the special circumstances of Shanghai and ordered strict enforcement and diligent collection. Our association immediately convened a temporary general meeting of members and resolved to reapply, according to the law and based on the facts, listing six reasons for tax exemption. We also checked the fourth item of the principles and methods for reducing and exempting business tax promulgated by the Executive Yuan in December last year decided by the 47th National Affairs Conference, which states that for domestic native products and handicrafts related to the livelihoods of the poor, which need to be promoted and maintained under special circumstances in international trade, the manufacturing industry or sales industry may be appropriately reduced or exempted from business tax by the central government or the provincial and municipal governments. We prepared a memorial and recommended Zhang Yunzhi, Du Yunxiang, and Tao Yumen as representatives to go to the capital to petition the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry for exemption. Both department chiefs received them and believed that the reasons for requesting tax exemption were sufficient and in line with the fourth item of the principles and methods for reducing and exempting business tax promulgated by the 47th National Affairs Conference. Later, we requested the province to review and reply. Unexpectedly, after nearly a month, we received instructions from the Jiangsu Provincial Government, stating that the four methods for reducing and exempting business tax ordered by the Executive Yuan were somewhat obstructive to the situation in this province and had been reported for approval and compliance, and ordered to be informed. Our association immediately continued to argue on the basis of the previous case. It happened that the Shanghai war broke out suddenly, and this case was shelved without recovery. Unexpectedly, we recently received an order from the Jiangsu Provincial Government, according to the reply from the Finance Office, which stated that the situation of lace is completely different from that of homespun cloth. Homespun cloth is supplied and demanded by the poor, and tax exemption is still reasonable. Lace, on the other hand, is close to luxury goods and has nothing to do with the livelihoods of the poor, so there is no need for tax exemption. We were ordered to fill in the report and pay taxes within a limited time. After receiving the order, our association believed that the reply from the Finance Office was not only ignorant of the actual situation of Philie lace but also completely ignored the provisions of the fourth item of the principles and methods for reducing and exempting business tax decided and promulgated by the 47th National Affairs Conference, which states that native products and handicrafts related to the livelihoods of the poor, which need to be promoted and maintained under special circumstances in international trade, may be appropriately reduced or exempted from tax. We again recounted the actual situation of Philie lace manufacturing and the gradual reduction of exports, based on the 47th National Affairs Conference and the Shanghai tax exemption precedent, and continued to separately petition, stating at the end of the memorial that this case is a purely legal request made by merchants based on government orders and precedents. No matter how strictly the tax authorities force the collection, merchants will ultimately be unable to bear this deformed burden that violates the tax exemption precedent and is close to being biased. We have exhausted our voices, and it is still unknown whether we can invite the provincial government authorities to show special pity and approve our request. However, our association believes that the decline of Philie lace has reached an extreme degree, and exports are gradually shrinking. If we are taxed at 5 per mille of the business turnover, the cost will increase, and it will be even more difficult to maintain business. Most of those who operate this industry are short of capital, so how can they survive, and hundreds of thousands of poor women in our Pudong, on whom they depend for a living, will also be desperate. The importance of the relationship is not falsely stated. Because we believe that your association is a Pudong fellow townsmen group with deep qualifications and prestige, and especially values the suffering of merchants, we are specially recounting the case and copying all the previous memorials and instructions to inform you. We hope that you will examine the matter and grant us your strong support so as to achieve the goal of tax exemption and benefit our industry. To the Pudong Fellow Townsmen Association."

The French Concession Public Works Bureau Levies a Business Tax on Solid Fuel 132

Negotiations and Solutions Have Been Reached by the Taxpayers' Association

Six Yuan Changed to Two Yuan

Implemented on July 1st

The French Concession Public Works Bureau has issued new regulations for the management of solid fuel warehouses and businesses, levying an annual business tax of six yuan, divided into two installments of three yuan each. The Coal Industry Association sent a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, which forwarded a letter to the French Concession Public Works Bureau, appealing for the revocation of the tax, but it was ineffective. The Bureau also sent personnel to implement the tax separately. Except for a few small coal and charcoal shops run by women who mistakenly paid the tax, all coal shops unanimously refused to pay and jointly signed a public petition to Director General Tranel, demanding that he withdraw the order and revoke the tax. It has been reported in previous reports that this case was handled by Zhang Gengshan (Manager of Jin Shun Sen Shun Jin Shun San Coal Shops), Chairman of the United Association of Merchants on the 12th Road of the New West District of the French Concession, who stated that the tax was really difficult for the industry to bear and requested assistance from the Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the French Concession. The Taxpayers' Association convened a meeting to discuss and decided to recommend Shang Mujian and Cheng Zhusun as representatives to repeatedly visit Director General Tranel with Zhang Gengshan to negotiate. Director General Tranel ordered the tax collectors to stop collecting the tax and submitted the original case to the Board of Directors for reconsideration and discussion to reduce the burden on the coal shops. As a result, the business tax of the business was reduced by four yuan from the original six yuan per year to two yuan, and it was still divided into two installments for collection, and it was postponed to July 1st for implementation. However, the directors of the Public Works Bureau considered the situation of the warehouse business tax to be special and still followed the original proposal. Director General Tranel informed the Taxpayers' Association of the reduction and postponement in a letter. The Taxpayers' Association immediately replied to Zhang Gengshan, and Zhang Gengshan separately informed the coal shops in the Concession. It is said that the coal shops have also understood and expressed their willingness to pay the tax and thanked Zhang Gengshan for his enthusiasm and Shang Mujian and Cheng Zhusun for their willingness to help. Therefore, the case has now been resolved.

Original Situation: The Zhabei Defense Corps originally had eight squadrons, each with 108 people led by a captain. Including the affiliated teams, there were more than a thousand people. Active Replenishment: After the Japanese troops withdrew from Zhabei, our side immediately took over, and our side's security围 immediately registered. If there were any incomplete ones, they were replenished. However, the Peiping-Shanghai route, running parallel to the Jinpu Railway, failed to gain traction and was soon suspended. According to Wu Zhaoxuan, the company's secretary, speaking to a Central News Agency reporter, the company is now actively preparing the Shanghai-Tianjin route. Originally planned for seaplanes, the high salinity of the seawater in that area would damage the aircraft. Therefore, land-based aircraft will be used instead. The route will run from Shanghai, through Haizhou and Qingdao, to Tianjin, a total distance of 664 nautical miles. The flight from Shanghai to Tianjin will take seven hours. Airfields in Haizhou and Tianjin are already fully prepared. However, because the airfield in Qingdao has been leased to the Japanese, Liu Peiquan, the company's manager, along with Aviation Director Band, and Deputy Director Nie Kaiyi, etc., are scheduled to fly to Qingdao tomorrow (i.e., today) to negotiate. A resolution is expected, and passenger service should formally begin next month.

Establishment of the Electric Company Labor Union 139

Workers at the Shanghai Electric Company, enraged by the factory's dismissal of 121 workers on the first of last month and the violation of the terms agreed upon during the sale by the former Municipal Council, appointed representatives to negotiate repeatedly without success. In an effort to unite and resist effectively, the entire workforce of over 2,500 workers has been actively organizing a labor union. Preparations are now complete, and the inaugural meeting was held yesterday at 2:00 PM in the auditorium of the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce. Official directors and supervisors were elected, and several important resolutions were passed.

The meeting was attended by workers from both the old and new factories, Li Yongxiang and Li Mengnan from the General Labor Union, Zhou Xuexiang, Ye Xianggao, Liu Xinquan, Shao Xubai, Zhu Xizhang, Zhang Zizhi from various labor unions, and staff representative Fang Qian, totaling over 2,000 people. A five-member presidium (names temporarily withheld) was elected by public nomination. The chairman began by reporting that the workers were enraged by the employer's unwarranted dismissal of a large number of workers, and repeated demands for reinstatement were ignored. Now that the union's organization is complete, this inaugural meeting is being held to discuss countermeasures. This was followed by speeches from Li Yongxiang and Li Mengnan of the General Labor Union and representatives of various other unions (details omitted). Finally, union directors and supervisors were elected, and six important resolutions were passed.

Resolutions Passed: (1) Demand that the employer recognize the union's right to represent all workers. (2) Demand that the employer not dismiss workers without cause. (3) Workers who retire must be paid a retirement bonus of six months' salary and a pension equal to 5% of their full salary. (4) Demand that the employer provide a monthly subsidy of 500 yuan for union activities. (5) Each worker will initially contribute half a day's salary to the union's basic fund, and a fund management committee will be established. (6) Workers who are unjustly injured by foreigners demand compensation for medical expenses and assurance that similar incidents will not recur.

Yongchang Shipping Company Adds New Vessel to the Tongyang Line 141

The stretch of the Yangtze River downstream from Shanghai to Huajiaqiao in Yangzhou, known as the Tongyang Line (colloquially called the "Little Yangtze"), covers approximately 600 nautical miles and has 23 ports, more than the main Yangtze River. Consequently, business there is no less prosperous than on the main Yangtze. The route was originally served by the Dada and Datong companies, whose operations were thriving. Every year in late summer and early autumn, the Jiangbei area produces a large quantity of miscellaneous grains, and the scheduled sailings were insufficient to meet demand. Therefore, the two companies would add direct service ships to carry cargo at that time. Now, Meng Zhaoyue and his younger brother Zhuoran have initiated the organization of the Yongfeng Shipping Company to join the Tongyang Line. Preparations have been underway for four months, and the company began operations last Saturday. The company originally planned to operate three vessels. It has now purchased one vessel, named Yongchang, with a total tonnage of over 500 tons and a passenger capacity of over 300. It is docked at Pier No. 8 in Nanshi and departs from Shanghai every Wednesday and Saturday. Zhuoran has been appointed the manager of the company, and Chen Fangru has been appointed the business director.

Renji Hospital Annual Report 142

Renji Hospital on Shandong Road, established 85 years ago, is one of the earliest hospitals in Shanghai. Last winter, the new building was completed, and the facilities have been further improved. The 85th annual report has recently been released. Last year, there were a total of 133,228 outpatient visits, involving approximately 54,000 people, and 2,818 inpatients. There were a total of 9,394 emergency cases, including 8,008 men and 1,386 women and children. There were 1,155 attempted suicides, including 509 men and 646 women. 629 physical examinations were conducted, and the X-ray department performed 1,860 diagnoses and took 3,280 images. The total donations received from Chinese individuals throughout the year were 8,486 yuan, 6 jiao, and 25 liang, plus 4,236 yuan, 5 jiao, and 2 fen, plus 5,100 liang and 4 qian 9 fen from Westerners. Total expenditures for the year amounted to 215,000 liang, 3 qian, and 5 fen. However, income fell short of expenditures by 56,495 liang, 3 qian, and 3 fen.

Special Shipping News 143

Changes in the Yangtze River Channel: A notice from the Jianghai Customs states that the port near Zhendu Fort in Zhenjiang has become silted up. The lightships established at the central sandbar east entrance and west entrance of the port have been removed. All Yangtze River steamers are hereby notified to pay attention when navigating upstream and downstream. In addition, the Jiuduan lightship, which is located in the waters within Chuansha, has been replaced by a lightship temporarily dispatched by the Customs to benefit shipping merchants, although a new lightship has not yet been sent.

Steamship Bureau Collects Water Fees in Cash: Since the war, all industries in Shanghai have been impacted. The losses incurred by import and export customs brokers have also been significant. Jardine Matheson's Chongqing branch has temporarily suspended operations, and a certain Shandong-based customs broker recently went bankrupt, incurring losses of over 100,000 yuan, with various steamship companies having outstanding water fees. Yesterday, the Shanghai branch of the British firm Jardine Matheson decided that, starting on the 25th of this month, all export goods declared by customs brokers must be paid for in cash and no longer on credit.

Japanese Military Attaché Arrives in Shanghai: Lieutenant Colonel Kita Hagine, specially dispatched by the Japanese General Staff, has arrived in Shanghai to take over as military attaché at the Japanese Consulate-General in Shanghai. Kita arrived on the Nagasaki Maru. Lieutenant Colonel Tanaka, Major Hirata, and others welcomed him upon arrival. Kita said that he had previously served in China six years ago and will immediately take office at the Donghe Foreign Firm.

Shipping Club: The Shanghai shipping industry has organized a shipping club to promote proper entertainment. The location is tentatively set at No. 10 Guangdong Road, in the Sanbei Housing Building. The Chinese insurance industry has also joined this club. The organizational fee has been agreed upon at 40,000 yuan, to be shared by shipping companies and insurance companies. The number of basic members is set at 300, with the insurance industry nominating 50 members. The shipping association has notified the various shipping bureaus, which have already agreed. The building is currently being renovated.

City National Arts Center Welcomes Director Wu 144

The City National Arts Center held a grand banquet at the Central Western Restaurant the evening before last (the 23rd) to welcome Director Wu Tiecheng and to solicit members for the fifth term. Present were Director Wu's representative Yin Rugeng, Lin Kanghou, Wang Yansong, and about 60 other people. Yuan Ludeng, the deputy director of the center, delivered a speech. This was followed by a report from Director Zhang Fucheng on the center's founding in 1928, the disruption caused by the January 28th Incident, the current reorganization, and plans for future work. Yin's representative then gave a reply, and Lin Kanghou and Wang Yansong gave speeches as well. The gist of their remarks was that China's national strength is weak, and foreign aggression is rampant. The biggest reason for this is the lack of physical well-being among the people. If we want to talk about saving the country in the future, we must first strengthen ourselves. The most effective way to strengthen oneself is to practice national arts. National arts are invented and cultivated by our Chinese nation thousands of years ago and are beneficial to the body in ways that other forms of exercise cannot match. After the speeches, the banquet began. Subsequently, instructors of the center, Tong Zhongyi, Wu Jianquan, Ma Yueliang, and others performed various techniques to add to the occasion. The sword lights flashed, and the cold air was chilling. The gathering finally ended in joy.

Minhang Town Plans to Build Summer Resort Garden 146

Shanghai-Minhang Bus Company Adds Special Buses Minhang Town, located southwest of the city, is more than 80 li from Shanghai. The town is a prosperous commercial center bordering the Huangpu River. In the past, the local magnate, Mr. Li Yingshi, raised large sums of money to purchase land and build the Shanghai-Minhang Motor Road, facilitating transportation. He also built Min Garden north of the town, with artificial hills and flowers, which were of particular interest. Amusement facilities were set up inside, and during the summer months, Chinese and foreign people from Shanghai would flock there during their leisure time. Last summer, the town opened the Riverside Garden on the bank of the Huangpu River at the southern end of the Shanghai-Minhang Road. The garden had a tennis court, swimming pool, Western restaurant, etc., and was extremely popular with tourists. Since the cessation of the Shanghai War, many people from Shanghai have been taking buses to Minhang for sightseeing. Therefore, a large Shanghai merchant is now rebuilding the former site of the Riverside Garden into a summer resort garden. Construction began several months ago and is now nearing completion. The garden has a beautiful location and stunning scenery, with clean air that is beneficial to health. The prospect of successful business is assured. It is also learned that the Shanghai-Minhang Bus Company is preparing to add special buses, which are scheduled to begin running next week or at the opening.

Aftermath of the Factional Fighting Near the Second District 147

Li Xinzai Accuses the Second District of Unjust Punishment

Mediation Is Underway, and Peaceful Resolution Is Expected

A few days ago, a crowd fight involving more than 100 Shanghai hoodlums took place at the Changle Tea House, located just a stone's throw away from the Second District Police Station in Nanshi. Each side carried a large number of axes and iron rulers, and the fighting was intense, with many people seriously injured. At the time, the area around Wansheng Bridge was on the verge of chaos, and traffic was completely blocked. When the Second District police finally arrived, they only intercepted a small number of people, including Li Xinzai, and seized several axes. At the time, District Chief Zhang Dongkai, in addition to sending the injured to the hospital, immediately interrogated Li Xinzai. According to Li, he worked as a ticket seller for the French tram company, and he explained the cause of the altercation. District Chief Zhang, in a fit of rage, believed that Li and others dared to incite a crowd and carry weapons in broad daylight, within earshot of the police station, and that they would be responsible if anyone died as a result. Therefore, he had Li severely beaten before handing him over to the District Court. That evening, the court temporarily released Li on bail pending trial. It is now reported that the case has ended. However, Li Xinzai feels aggrieved that the Second District Police Station should not have used unjust punishment. He intends to hire lawyer Xu Heling to file a lawsuit in the District Court against District Chief Zhang. It is now reported that District Chief Zhang, in order to settle the matter, has had someone named Zhang come forward to mediate, agreeing to compensate Li for the medical expenses incurred as a result of the injuries sustained from the beating, and to express his apologies. It is reported that Li is satisfied and has agreed to a peaceful resolution.

County Requires Party Fees on Property Deeds 150

The Shanghai County Finance Bureau, lacking funds for the county's Party affairs expenses for the 21st year, proposed levying one yuan per hundred yuan on the sale of land and property deeds and half a yuan per hundred yuan on pawn deeds. The proposal was immediately submitted to the County Administration Conference and approved. Director Wang then reported the situation to the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Finance for verification and clarification, stating that it would not hinder the regular tax revenue. The Provincial Department of Finance issued a directive approving the county's levy of one yuan per hundred yuan on the sale of deeds, but exempting the levy on pawn deeds. The bureau has issued an order to the Deed Tax Office to comply with the instructions.

Worker Commits Suicide After Being Denied Wages and Humiliated by His Employer 156

Shen Dingnian, age 55, from Chongming, was introduced by his fellow villager Lu Ziming to work for a Mr. Shen at Caojia Muqiao in Wusong one year ago. It was agreed that his salary would be 5 yuan per month. After one year and one month, a total of 65 yuan had not been paid. During the January 28th Incident, the residents of Wusong fled, and Shen also returned to his hometown to take refuge. After the Japanese army withdrew and Wusong gradually returned to normal, Shen sent his younger brother and son, Haiqiao, to Mr. Shen's house to demand his wages. However, Mr. Shen intended to renege on the debt and falsely claimed that Shen Ding had already settled his wages when he left. He gathered a crowd and beat the two men, who fled back to their hometown and told Shen Ding everything. Shen was shocked to hear this. A few days ago, he bought a table and came to Shanghai, staying at his fellow villager's house. Yesterday morning, he went to Mr. Shen's house alone to demand his wages but was humiliated and falsely accused of lacking several pieces of furniture, which he was ordered to compensate for. As a result, he left in displeasure without receiving any money. After Shen Ding left Mr. Shen's house, he felt infinite anger. He walked to Songzhen, bought opium paste, secretly ingested it, and then went to his introducer, Lu Ziming, and explained everything. After a while, Lu noticed that his face was pale and his spirits were low. Upon questioning him strictly, Shen told him everything, finally admitting that he had committed suicide by taking poison. Lu hired a car and sent him to Tongren Hospital for treatment, but it was ineffective. He died at 5:20 PM.

Young Woman Hangs Herself Over Haircut 160

The young woman, Chen Lushi, age 24, from Tianjin, was beautiful. Her husband, Chen Zhiwei, age 22, used to work at a foreign firm but is now unemployed. They had been married for over a year and lived together at No. 17 Qingyuli, South Chengdu Road. They were quite well-off. At 10:30 AM the day before yesterday, Chen hanged herself alone in her bedroom with a silk ribbon suspended from the bed. Chen Su Shi (the husband's grandmother, age 76), saw her and called Chen Zhiwei to help her down. However, she was already barely breathing and could not be saved. Chen Zhiwei and others reported the incident to the Xinzha Police Station, who ordered detective Ye Yushan to investigate. The deceased was sent to Renji Hospital and then to the Forensic Pathology Laboratory on Feilun Road for an autopsy. My wife cut her hair two weeks ago, but my father-in-law is from a traditional family and works on a boat. My wife was afraid that her father would quarrel with her if he saw it, so she…" The brother of the deceased, Chen Jin, age 22, who resides at No. 54 Yuanjili, Tangshan Road, and is currently a student, said, "My sister and brother-in-law have always been on very good terms. This time, she really committed suicide because of the haircut." After hearing the statements, Guo concluded that the deceased, Chen Lushi, had committed suicide by hanging herself and that the body should be returned to her husband, Chen Zhiwei, for burial.

The Case of a Foreigner Inducing Sex with Chinese Male and Female Servants 161

Zhang Songlin from Ningbo is currently twenty-one years old. He was working as a houseboy at the residence of a foreigner at No. 114, Lane 7, Nanyang Road. Earlier this month, the foreigner also hired a Suzhou woman named Xue A’e as an "amah" (nursemaid). Zhang, seeing that Xue possessed some beauty, immediately attempted to seduce her. However, Xue was only seventeen, her affections just opening. After Zhang’s enticements, she couldn’t help but feel a flutter in her heart. Just as their passion was reaching a fever pitch, Zhang was suddenly dismissed by his master. Unwilling to give up the meat that was already at his mouth, he secretly snuck into Xue’s bedroom the following night (the thirteenth of last month) to fulfill his amorous dreams. After that, Zhang continued to visit her secretly for romantic encounters, about seven or eight times in total. However, he eventually felt that this furtive, secret behavior was inconvenient. Therefore, around 9 PM on the thirteenth of this month, he went to Xue again and told her, "The wages here are too low. I've already recommended you for a job at a foreigner's house at No. 2 Tangshan Road. The wages are much better there, so go quickly." Xue, unaware of his deception, followed him out. She was then taken to the building of the Yangshupu Electric Company to stay overnight at the home of his mother, Zhang Huangshi. The next day, they rented a house at No. 429, Siwen Lane, Dalian Bay Road, and began living together. However, Xue Fengshi, Xue’s mother, thought that A’e, having just arrived in Shanghai, had gone out shopping and lost her way home after her daughter disappeared. She reported it to the police station, saying that her daughter was lost. It wasn't until the afternoon of the day before yesterday that she discovered that her daughter had actually been seduced and abducted by Zhang Songlin. She then reported it to the police station, which dispatched Detective Fan Defu and Patrolman Hu Zhiyun. They first arrested Zhang's mother, Huangshi, and then, guided by her, went to Siwen Lane and arrested Zhang Songlin, rescuing Xue A’e at the same time. They were all taken back to the Jing’an Temple Police Station. Xue was ordered to be sent to the Red Cross Hospital to verify that her hymen had been ruptured. Consequently, Zhang and his mother were taken into custody separately. Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the Second Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. According to the police lawyer, Qian Xunjiu, he recounted the previous events and said that the two defendants were being prosecuted for violating Article 257, Section 2 of the Criminal Law, the crime of disrupting a family. Then, according to the victim, Xue A’e, she complained that Zhang had used the pretext of recommending a job to have sexual relations with her several times. Furthermore, according to Xue Fengshi, her daughter A’e was seventeen years old, born in the eighth month of the lunar calendar. She had been betrothed to someone in her hometown of Suzhou before coming to Shanghai. Now that she had been violated by the defendant, she demanded an investigation. Zhang Songlin and Zhang Huangshi stammered in their confessions. After Judge Wu Tingqi verified the confessions in court, he sentenced Zhang Songlin to one year of imprisonment for intending to commit sexual intercourse with a woman under the age of twenty and inducing her to leave the control of a person with parental rights. Zhang Huangshi was sentenced to six months of imprisonment for aiding and abetting the harboring of the induced person, both sentences suspended for three years. Xue A’e was released to her mother.

Soldiers Causing Trouble at Xiashi Station 162

The twelve detained soldiers arrived at Xiashi Station yesterday at around 11:00 AM on the 36th slow train from Shanghai to Hangzhou. There were more than twenty wounded soldiers from the 88th Division in the third-class carriage. Because they were traveling without tickets, a conflict arose with the military police escorting the train. The wounded soldiers immediately used teacups and utensils from the carriage to hurl at the heads of the military police. Because they were outnumbered, the military police were struck on the head, and blood flowed freely. At that time, the 31st express train from Hangzhou to Shanghai arrived at Xiashi Station. The stationmaster immediately ordered the train to stop and boarded the carriage to report to the military police escort and requested assistance in suppressing the unrest. The wounded soldiers were still committing violence, so they surrounded the wounded soldiers and fired shots as a warning, capturing twelve of the troublemaking soldiers on the spot. They were escorted back to Hangzhou for questioning on the original train. When the military police fired, the passengers on both trains got off the train and fled. Fortunately, the situation was resolved quickly, and no passengers were injured, but they were quite frightened.

Record of the Shanghai-Taicang Bus Company Shareholders' Meeting 163

The Shanghai-Taicang Long-Distance Bus Company held its twelfth annual shareholders' meeting yesterday at 2:00 PM at the Ningbo Native Place Association on Xizang Road. At 5:30 PM, a vote was held to elect two supervisors. Gu Zhenyi received 17,111 votes, and Huang Qiusheng received 15,813 votes. Both were elected. Publication of (Guide to Touring Beijing, Zhenjiang, Suzhou, and Wuxi) 167

Geographer Chen Rizhang recently compiled the book (Guide to Touring Beijing, Zhenjiang, Suzhou, and Wuxi). It describes the transportation, lodging, scenic spots, historical sites, and other items of the four famous regions in detail. It is quite clear and new. It includes four large colored maps, which are not only convenient for touring but also provide historical and geographical reference materials. The entire book is 170,000 words, finely bound in a thick volume, priced at eight silver dollars, with a special price of 20% off. Opening of the Paris Open-Air Cinema 168

The film industry in this city inevitably suffers a decline during the summer months. The reason for this is that most people in the industry are unaccustomed to sitting in dark and airless movie theaters during the hot weather. Therefore, in recent years, some theaters have added air conditioning, while others have established open-air cinemas specifically for summer operations. Recently, an organization called the Paris Open-Air Cinema was established in the Paris Night Garden, across from the Zhaofeng Garden. The equipment and layout are very perfect, and a large sum of money was used to install a sound machine from the Western Electric Company of the United States, exclusively showing selected Chinese and foreign sound blockbusters. Last night was the first day of the opening, and the latest sensational Paramount blockbuster, "The Love Parade," directed by Ernst Lubitsch and starring Maurice Chevalier and Jeanette MacDonald, was specially screened. Admission was uniformly priced at one yuan, and the audience was extraordinarily crowded. The reason for this is that the venue is surrounded by flowers and trees, the air is fresh, and the oppressive heat does not reach it, making it a summer resort for Shanghai's dancers. The venue also has a reception area next to the Palace Grand Theater of the New World Hotel. Lilli Motor Company is contracted to provide cars to pick up guests every night from 8:30 PM to 9:00 PM, charging only thirty cents per person. The original dancing will continue as usual after the movie ends at 11:00 PM, and no tickets will be sold.

Residents of Daode Lane Oppose Demolition of Houses 169

Shen Shumei, the landlord of Daode Lane on Cadre Road, usually entrusts the foreign firm Peace & Ming to collect rent for the lane. Recently, he issued notices using the pretext of rebuilding, ordering all residents to move out. The residents are extremely angry, all saying that the suffering of the market closure and unemployment after the January 28th Incident has not yet recovered, and the landlord's actions are too cruel. Moreover, the houses are still in good condition and do not need to be rebuilt. Therefore, they have elected nine representatives, including He, Zhang, Shao, and Su, and entrusted lawyer Yu Hualong to make demands to the landlord. If the demands are not met, hundreds of residents will be forced to sleep in front of the landlord's door and cry for help, regardless of the consequences.

Xiao Renyuan's "Records of German Railway Investigation" 170

Xiao Renyuan, the former director of the Pinghan Railway Bureau, was sent by the central government to Europe and the United States three years ago to investigate railway operations. Xiao first went to Germany and studied at the University of Berlin. Afterwards, he went to various major railway companies in England, the United States, France, and Switzerland to intern. He has now started his journey back to China and has first written a large volume of "Records of German Railway Investigation." The content is extremely rich, detailing the latest German railway management, traffic, engineering, machinery, and accounting, chapter by chapter, collecting everything without omission. It contains more than one hundred tables and fifty exquisite diagrams. An appendix on world transportation provides a detailed overview of the transportation situation in various countries, which can serve as a compass for China's future railway development. It is said that the book has already been published and is being distributed by the Shanghai Life Weekly Society.

Basic Principles of Railway Transportation Regulations (Continued) Zheng Baozhao 173

(6) Uncompensated transport: For example, if a plaintiff and his luggage are transported by the defendant without compensation, and the luggage is lost in transit, the plaintiff demands compensation. However, the court believes that the defendant should not be held liable as an insurer or common carrier. This argument is quite fair, because if someone providing transportation services without compensation were to bear the special responsibility of insurance, it would be too unfair. However, if a transportation service appears to be free on the surface but is actually charging indirectly, the responsibility of a common carrier cannot be avoided.

(7) Transportation without a fixed fee should not be considered uncompensated: A carrier cannot avoid the responsibility of an insurer simply because it did not explicitly charge a fee at the time of carriage, nor can it avoid this responsibility by waiving the fee after the loss has occurred. Allowing them to avoid this would allow carriers to take the opportunity to evade the responsibilities of a common carrier. (To be continued)

Free Talk

Loving to Burn, Loving to Kill 174

One thing is worth noting: the study of European and Asian cultures seems to have started simultaneously. When Western Greek philosophy began to flourish, with Plato and Aristotle lecturing one after another, China was in the late Three Dynasties, the Spring and Autumn period, and the Warring States period, leading to the Qin and Han dynasties. The writings of the philosophers were also extremely popular at that time. Although Emperor Qin Shi Huang burned books and buried scholars alive, he could not stop the transmission of the philosophers' doctrines. When Cicero became a prominent figure in Rome, Han dynasty essays also reached their peak. Rome unified Europe, and the Western Han dynasty almost unified Asia. During the Song dynasty, there was alchemy, and during the Middle Ages, alchemy and magic were also extremely popular in the West. From this fact of the mutual communication of Eastern and Western cultures, we can understand that human intelligence does not vary according to race.

The places where Eastern and Western cultures communicate are too numerous to mention! For example, Emperor Qin Shi Huang built the Great Wall and the Epang Palace, while Rome was also engaged in large-scale construction projects. The luxury of the Epang Palace, as described in the "Rhapsody on the Epang Palace," is vividly remembered, but unfortunately, it was burned down by Xiang Yu in a single fire, leaving posterity with no way to admire or mourn it. In fact, the value of Chinese culture is often squandered by the general public. Throughout history, most cultural constructions have suffered the calamity of burning and killing. Countries with long-standing cultures often have many people who love to burn and kill, and these people who love to burn and kill continue for generations, accumulating like alluvial deposits. How can even the slightest cultural accumulation withstand the burning and killing of generations?

Speaking of the Epang Palace, during the Xianfeng period, there was a British minister to China named Thomas Wade, who was inspired to do research on it. Wade's Chinese was very good, and he even wrote a Chinese textbook for the British to read. According to Wade's research, in the garden of the Epang Palace, there were boats made of mercury and ducks and geese made of gold and silver. The bridges were made of copper wire mesh, making them soft and comfortable to walk on. However, since the Epang Palace was burned down by the ruthless Xiang Yu, even if Wade described it in flowery terms, there is no real evidence to prove it.

The Scientific War of the Twentieth Century 175

— Renwu

The war of the twentieth century is purely scientific, that is, chemical. As for airplanes, twenty years ago they were only an ideal. The "Eastern Miscellany" exaggerated the claims about new airships. Unexpectedly, in the Battle of Zhabei this time, the Japanese relied on airplanes to drop bombs, turning the destroyed Zhabei into scorched earth. Doesn't China also have airplanes? In the Battle of Zhengzhou, they were quite effective. Knowing that Chinese airplanes were coming to Shanghai, the Japanese went to Suzhou to intercept them. In this aerial war, the American Short was killed, and Japanese soldiers were also killed and wounded. There was also a dawn battle over the Qiantang River. Thus, the war of airplanes will inevitably become a vanguard for the masters of the Pacific. Anti-aircraft guns are the opponents of airplanes. But there are people who said that the "Flying Thunder," invented by Cai Linsheng (is already successful, and has good results.) Others say that it is just propaganda. The Flying Thunder is just a "Flying Heaven Thunder," with a short range that cannot shoot down airplanes. If there really were Flying Thunder, why is there no record of it? Both statements have their reasons. I only hope that Cai Linsheng will continue to research and will surely succeed one day.

The types of poison gas manufactured by various countries total more than two hundred. The ones made in Czechoslovakia are particularly ingenious. Although Japan claimed that it had not used them in the Battle of Zhabei in Shanghai, the fact that the ones made in Czechoslovakia were bought by Japan is true. In the future, the use of poison gas is inevitable. The Chinese army should not worry about Japan's use of poison gas, but should worry that we cannot invent a powerful weapon to defend against poison gas. Dumdum bullets have already been proven in hospitals. Smoke bombs have already been seen in Yunzaobang and Liuhang. Light and heavy tanks are even speeding between Wusong and Jiangwan. Only the invention of the "death ray" has been rumored, but it has not yet been seen in battle. As for Japan's newly invented torpedoes, they will surely dominate the Pacific in the future. China

Record of Seizing a Gun 176

— Xuelang

During the Sino-Japanese war in Shanghai, I often went back and forth to the battlefield as a reporter. Sometimes the front lines were quiet, and I would remember my friends in the trenches. We would sit knee-to-knee on the ground and talk about snippets of news from the war. Someone told me about seizing a gun. The story was very interesting. During the fierce battle at Baziqiao, our army counterattacked. An advance suicide squad of fourteen men, carrying bombs, rushed into the enemy's ranks. At that time, twenty enemies were guarding a machine gun. Seeing our army approaching, they retreated in a panic without firing a shot. Our army captured the machine gun without firing a single bullet and then used the gun to sweep the enemy. Not one of the enemies who had previously guarded the gun was spared. Using their own methods to treat their own bodies, that's what it's all about. Now that the situation in Rehe is urgent, I am writing this to encourage the brave soldiers who defend our country.

has only receiving and sending government officials, so torpedoes and submarines have to sigh that heroes have no place to use their skills.
